Why the Proof from Power Fails Against the Mu'tazila
Al-Nasafi explains the limited scope of proofs based on God's power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the argument from God's power to endorse monotheism does not decisively refute dualism according to the Mu'tazila, and how it remains valid within Maturidi principles.

Core Idea
Proofs based on God's power are only as strong as the underlying assumptions about who creates actions.

Al-Nasafi has been presenting proofs for the oneness of God based on the nature of power and creation. However, he now steps back to note a crucial methodological point: these proofs are not accepted by the Mu'tazila. Their belief that humans independently create their own actions means that God's power can be 'overridden' without diminishing His divinity, thus the proof does not force them to reject two creators. Let us see his exact reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through. Then read the translation to catch the flow of the argument.
Notice the key phrase 'يستقيمان على أصول المعتزلة' (are not valid upon the principles of the Mu'tazila).
2
Understand the Mu'tazila position
The passage explains why the proof fails: because according to the Mu'tazila, when a human agent creates an action, God's power over that specific act ceases, yet God remains divine. This is the core of their objection.
The example of movement in an animal's limb illustrates the point.
3
See the analogy with two creators
Al-Nasafi extends the argument: if one creator incapacitates another in some action, that does not negate the other's divinity. So the proof from power does not refute dualism for the Mu'tazila.
4
Contrast with Ahl al-Sunna principles
The final sentence clarifies that the proof is only valid on our (Maturidi/Sunni) principles where God is the sole creator. This contrast reinforces the importance of theological premises.
Reflect on why the disagreement about human action leads to such different conclusions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذان الوجهان من الدلالة لا يستقيمان على أصول المعتزلة فإن حركة ما يوجدها الحيوان باختياره كان الله تعالى قبل وجودها عالما بها قادرا على إيجادها فإذا أوجدها الحيوان على أصولهم واستبد بإيجاده، زالت قدرة الله تعالى عنه، وكذا كان الله تعالى قادرا على إيجاد حركة في عضو من أعضاء الحيوان، فإذا أوجد الحيوان السكون فيه زالت قدرة الله تعالى عن إيجاد الحركة فيه، ومع ذلك لم تزل ألوهيته تعالى بتعجيز غيره إياه، فكذا إذا كانا اثنين وعجز أحدهما صاحبه عن شيء ما لم تزل ربوبيته وألوهيته، وإنما يستقيم ذلك على أصولنا، والله الهادي إلى الصواب.
And these two aspects of proof are not valid upon the principles of the Mu'tazila. For the movement that an animal originates by his choice, Allah was knowing of it before its existence, able to bring it about. When the animal originates it according to their principles and is independent in bringing it about, Allah's power over it ceases. Likewise, Allah was able to bring about movement in a limb of the animal's limbs, but when the animal originates rest in it, Allah's power over bringing about movement in it ceases, and despite that, His divinity does not cease due to another's incapacitation of Him. Thus, if there were two [creators] and one incapacitates the other from something, His lordship and divinity would not cease. But that is only valid upon our principles. And Allah is the guide to rightness.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a methodological note explaining why the proofs based on power (qudra) do not work against the Mu'tazila. The author states that these two proofs are not valid on Mu'tazila principles. The reason is that the Mu'tazila believe that humans create their own actions independently. For example, when an animal originates a movement by its choice, according to the Mu'tazila, Allah knew and was able to bring it about, but once the animal actualizes it, Allah's power over that movement ceases. Yet Allah's divinity does not cease because of this incapacitation by another (the animal). Similarly, if there were two creators, one could incapacitate the other, but that would not nullify divinity. Thus, the proof from power does not decisively refute dualism on Mu'tazila grounds. However, the author clarifies that it does hold on the principles of Ahl al-Sunna (Maturidi), where Allah alone is the creator of all actions.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
أصول
الاستبداد
القدرة
الألوهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the proof from God's power is a universally accepted argument for oneness.
Correction: This passage shows that the proof is only conclusive given certain assumptions about human action; the Mu'tazila reject it because they believe humans create their own actions, allowing God's power to be 'overridden' without affecting His divinity.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the proof from power is not valid against the Mu'tazila?
A) Because the Mu'tazila deny the existence of God.
B) Because the Mu'tazila believe humans create their own actions, so God's power can cease without affecting His divinity.
C) Because the Mu'tazila accept the proof but reinterpret it.
D) Because the Mu'tazila do not believe in power as an attribute.

Key Takeaway
Theological arguments rely on shared premises; the proof from God's power only refutes dualism if one holds that God alone creates all actions, as the Maturidis do, not if one holds that humans create their own acts, as the Mu'tazila do.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever presented a logical argument for a belief, only to realize the other person did not share your starting assumptions? How does Al-Nasafi's admission that the proof from power fails against the Mu'tazila challenge you to examine the foundations of your own faith?
?
The Mu'tazila believed humans create their own actions, limiting God's power over those actions, yet they still considered Him divine. What does this reveal about how your own unexamined assumptions might be limiting your full recognition of Allah's absolute power and creativity?
?
Al-Nasafi states the proof only stands on 'our principles' (Ahl al-Sunna). Are you content to rely on proofs that work only within your own school, or are you willing to study and understand opposing views deeply enough to refute them from their own principles? What step will you take today to strengthen your knowledge of the foundations of your aqeedah?

Refuting the Mu'tazili Argument from Two Creators
Refutation of a Mu'tazili argument using rational analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Mu'tazili argument that affirming two creators leads to a logical contradiction.

Core Idea
One creator's action suffices; another's inaction does not create a contradiction.

The Mu'tazila argued that if there were two creators, the same object of power would lead to contradiction if one acts and the other refrains. The author responds by showing that the act of one creator alone makes the thing existent, and the other's inaction has no effect. An analogy with two men moving a log clarifies the point, demonstrating the weakness of the Mu'tazili reasoning. Pay attention to how the author uses everyday logic to uphold the possibility of multiple creators in the divine context, while affirming that in reality there is only one Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: the Mu'tazili argument is presented first, then the author's refutation with an analogy.
The passage begins by dismissing the Mu'tazili methods as weak before engaging with one specific argument.
2
Break down the Mu'tazili argument
Identify the steps of their reasoning: if two creators, each is powerful over the same thing; if one creates and the other refrains, the thing would be both existent and non-existent, which is impossible. Therefore, two creators cannot exist.
The contradiction they claim is that the object would be both 'performed and abandoned' simultaneously.
3
Understand the author's refutation
The author points out that if one creator brings the thing into existence, it becomes existent; the other's refraining does not make it non-existent. Non-existence before the act is irrelevant.
The key is that the inaction of the second creator does not negate the existence produced by the first.
4
Analyze the analogy
Two men who can move a log: if one moves it and the other does not, the log is moved. It does not remain in place because of the other's inaction. This illustrates that the act of one suffices.
The analogy is meant to show that the Mu'tazili claim of contradiction is based on a mistaken assumption.
5
Reflect on the lesson's takeaway
Consider how this argument demonstrates the use of rational judgment (hukm aqli) and analogy in kalam. The author defends the logical possibility of multiple creators, though theology affirms only one.
This is not affirming polytheism but refuting a flawed argument, so that tawhid can be established on sound reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أدلة للمعتزلة في الوحدانية ومناقشتها وتمسكوا بطرق ضعيفة لا طائل تحتها، ولا إمكان للتعويل عليها منها أنهم قالوا: لو كان للعالم صانعان لكان كل واحد منهما قادرا لنفسه ويكون مقدور كل واحد منهما مقدور الآخر، فيقتضي هذا أن يصح أن يفعل أحدهما ويترك الآخر فيكون مفعولا متروكا موجودا معدوما وهذا محال وإثبات صانعين يؤدي إلى هذا، والمؤدي إلى المحال محال، وهذا الاستدلال فاسد لأن أحدهما لو أوجده صار موجودا، ولا يكون معدوما بترك الآخر، والامتناع عن الفعل لأنه كان معدوما ولم يتعلق عدمه به ألا ترى أن رجلين لو كانا قادرين على نقل خشبة من مكان إلى مكان فنقلها أحدهما وترك الآخر نقلها صارت منقولة بنقل الناقل، ولم يبق في المكان الأول بترك الآخر نقله، فكذا هذا.
Arguments for the Mu'tazila concerning unity and their discussion. And they clung to weak methods, with no substance beneath them, and no possibility of relying upon them. Among them is that they said: If the world had two creators, each one of them would be powerful in himself, and the object of power of each one of them would be the object of power of the other. This necessitates that it be valid for one of them to act and the other to refrain, so that an act would be both performed and abandoned, existent and non-existent, and this is impossible. And affirming two creators leads to this, and that which leads to the impossible is impossible. But this reasoning is corrupt, because if one of them brought it into existence, it becomes existent, and it does not become non-existent by the other's refraining. And the abstention from the act is because it was non-existent and its non-existence was not attached to him. Do you not see that if two men were able to move a log from one place to another, and one of them moved it while the other refrained from moving it, it becomes moved by the mover's moving, and it does not remain in the first place because of the other's refraining from moving it. So likewise is this.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Mu'tazili argument against two creators. The author first presents the Mu'tazili position: they claim that if there were two creators, each would be powerful over the same thing, so if one creates and the other refrains, the thing would be both existent and non-existent, which is impossible. Therefore, affirming two creators is impossible. The author then refutes this by pointing out that if one creates, the object becomes existent; it is not rendered non-existent by the other's inaction. The non-existence before creation is irrelevant. He illustrates with an analogy: if two men can move a log, and one moves it while the other does not, the log is moved by the one who acted; it does not remain in its original place. Similarly, the act of one creator suffices, and the other's inaction does not create a contradiction.

Key Terms
صانعان
قادر
مقدور
مفعول متروك
موجود معدوم
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That if two creators existed, the same object would have to be both existent and non-existent simultaneously when one acts and the other refrains.
Correction: The object becomes existent by the act of one creator; the other's inaction does not produce non-existence. The alleged contradiction is based on a misunderstanding of causality.

Checkpoint
What does the author use as an analogy to refute the Mu'tazili argument that two creators lead to a contradiction?
A) Two kings ruling a single city
B) Two men moving a log, one acting and one refraining
C) Two scribes writing the same book
D) Two builders constructing a house

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili argument from two creators fails because the inaction of one creator does not negate the existence caused by the other; the act alone suffices, as shown by the log analogy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a truth about Allah because of a seemingly logical argument that you did not examine closely? This lesson reveals how even clever arguments can be flawed. Will you commit to studying the deeper proofs before accepting objections to your faith, or will you remain vulnerable to intellectual deception?
?
The Mu'tazili argument appears strong at first glance, but the refutation exposes its weakness. Where in your own life have you been swayed by an argument that sounded convincing but contradicted the clear teachings of Islam? What specific steps will you take to guard against such intellectual traps in the future?
?
The log analogy demonstrates that one creator's action is sufficient; the other's inaction changes nothing. Reflect: In your reliance on Allah, do you sometimes act as if your own efforts or the actions of others are necessary alongside His will? How can you deepen your tawhid in practical, daily actions so that you truly believe His act alone suffices?

Refuting the Mu'tazili Argument from Infinite Gods
Imam al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazili infinite-gods argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical flaw in the Mu'tazili argument that positing two gods leads to an infinite number of gods.

Core Idea
Finite plurality does not imply infinite regress.

The Mu'tazila argued that if two gods could exist, then any number could, leading to an infinite number of gods—an impossibility. Imam al-Nasafi refutes this by distinguishing between finite and infinite cases and by noting that even a single God's power does not necessitate infinite acts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Notice the logical structure: the Mu'tazili claim, then the refutation.
2
Identify the Mu'tazili argument
Find the premise: if two gods are possible, then any number is possible, leading to infinite gods and infinite acts, which is impossible.
This is the argument the author will refute.
3
Spot the author's counter-points
The author gives two refutations: (1) Even a single eternal being has infinite power but only finite acts occur; (2) The impossibility of infinite acts only applies if the number of gods is infinite, not finite.
Understand how these points dismantle the Mu'tazili reasoning.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The author concludes that to claim the impossibility for a finite number is gross ignorance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أنهم قالوا لو صح إثبات إلهين لصح إثبات آلهة لا نهاية لهم في العدد إذ لا عدد أولى من عدد ، ولو جاز إثبات آلهة لا يتناهون لجاز أن يفعل كل واحد منهم فعلا فيوجد من الأفعال ما لا نهاية له فى العدد، وهذا محال. فيقال لهم : إن الواحد من القدماء لا نهاية لمقدوره ومع ذلك لا يجوز أن يوجد بقدرته إلا ما يحصره العدد فكذا في القدماء، ولأن ما ذكرت من الاستحالة ثابت في القدماء بلا نهاية فأما في العدد المتناهي فلا تثبت تلك الاستحالة فينبغي أن يجوز ذلك وإبطال ما لا يثبت المحال بثبوته لإبطال ما ثبت المحال بثبوته جهل فاحش.
And among them is that they said: If the affirmation of two gods were valid, then the affirmation of gods without end in number would be valid, since no number is more appropriate than another. And if the affirmation of gods without limit were permissible, then it would be permissible for each one of them to perform an act, so that acts without end in number would come into existence, and this is impossible. So it is said to them: Indeed, the single one among the eternal beings has no limit to His power, yet only what number encompasses can come into existence by His power. So likewise with the eternal beings. And because the impossibility you mentioned is established in the case of eternal beings without limit; as for a finite number, that impossibility is not established. Therefore, that should be permissible. And to invalidate what does not establish the impossible by its affirmation, in order to invalidate what does establish the impossible by its affirmation, is gross ignorance.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage refutes a second Mu'tazili argument. The Mu'tazila argue: if two gods are possible, then any number is possible, leading to an infinite number of gods, which would produce infinite acts, which is impossible. Therefore, two gods are impossible. The author refutes by noting that even a single eternal being has infinite power, yet only a finite number of acts actually occur by His power. So the same applies when there are multiple eternal beings: the number of acts is limited, not infinite. Furthermore, the impossibility of infinite acts only applies if the number of gods is infinite; if the number is finite, the argument does not hold. To claim otherwise is ignorance.

Key Terms
آلهة لا نهاية
العدد المتناهي
العدد
استحالة
جهل فاحش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If two gods are possible, then an infinite number of gods must be possible.
Correction: Possibility of a finite number does not entail possibility of an infinite number; the argument conflates finite and infinite cases.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main point in refuting the Mu'tazili argument about infinite gods?
A) An infinite number of gods is impossible, so two gods are also impossible.
B) The possibility of a finite number of gods does not imply an infinite number.
C) Even a single god cannot produce infinite acts, so multiple gods cannot.
D) The Mu'tazila are ignorant of logic.

Key Takeaway
The possibility of a finite number of gods does not lead to an infinite regress; the Mu'tazili argument is invalid because it falsely assumes that finite possibility entails infinite possibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila assumed that if two gods were possible, then any number must be possible, ignoring the boundary between finite and infinite. In your own thinking, where have you carelessly extended a principle beyond its proper limits because it felt more logical, without checking where Allah has set boundaries?
?
The author calls the opposing argument 'gross ignorance.' Are you willing to have your cherished intellectual positions dismantled with such severity if they are wrong? What would it cost you to admit that a belief you held confidently was actually a logical fallacy?
?
This passage defends tawhid with razor-sharp reasoning. When you recite 'Lā ilāha illa Allāh,' do you feel the intellectual weight of its proof, or have you reduced it to a comfortable slogan? Ask yourself: if someone presented a clever argument against it, would you be equipped to respond, or would your faith rest only on habit?

Abu Hashim's Denial of Rational Proof for Tawhid
Presentation of Abu Hashim's position and objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu Hashim's claim that reason alone cannot prove God's unity and his objection to the proof of mutual prevention.

Core Idea
Reason is insufficient for tawhid: Abu Hashim's challenge to kalām.

When Abu Hashim became leader of the Mu'tazila, he found that on their principles, rational proof of God's unity was impossible. He therefore argued that only revelation can establish tawhid, and he attacked the famous proof of mutual prevention (dalīl al-tamānu'). This passage presents his objection in detail, setting the stage for the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read Abu Hashim's claim
Read the portion of the Arabic passage up to the point where the refutation begins (before 'قيل له'). Focus on his assertion that reason cannot prove unity and that we rely on revelation.
Notice his argument that if left to reason, we would deem two makers possible.
2
Understand his objection to dalīl al-tamānu'
He argues that the impossibility of mutual prevention in two gods is like the impossibility of certain actions in one God – not due to incapacity but due to inherent unsuitability.
He parallels the case of one God not being described as powerful over injustice.
3
Examine the universal will argument
On the assumption of universal will, he points out that two wills cannot contradict without contradicting known reality, thus making the objection stronger.
This is a subtle point about the coherence of will and knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[أبو هاشم ودلائل الوحدانية والرد عليه] فلما انتهت نوبة رئاسة المعتزلة إلى أبي هاشم ورأى تعذر إثبات الوحدانية بالدلائل العقلية على أصولهم الفاسدة وتحير سلفه في ذلك، فزعم أن لا دلالة في العقل على وحدانية الصانع، وإنا عرفنا أن الصانع واحد بدلالة السمع دون العقل، ولو خلينا وعقولنا لجوزنا أن يكون للعالم صانعان فأكثر واشتغل بالاعتراض على دلالة التمانع التي هي أشهر دلالات أهل التوحيد فزعم أن قدرتهما أو قدرة أحدهما على ما أوردتموه يخرجهما أو أحدهما عن الربوبية فدخل هذا في جملة المستحيلات التي لا يوصف أحدهما بالقدرة عليه ولا بالعجز عنه كما منعتموه في الواحد من الوصف بالقدرة على الظلم والكذب وسائر الأوصاف التي لا تليق بالباري عز وجل، ومن الوصف بالعجز عنها للاستحالة فكذا يعتذرون في الاثنين قال: ونوضحه على قول من يقول بتعميم الإرادة في الكائنات، أن الإرادة لا تخالف عندهم المعلوم، والمعلوم لا يخالف الكائن، فكيف يتوهم من أحدهما إرادة خلاف صاحبه وفي إرادة خلاف صاحبه خلاف معلومة، قيل له: إن أول ما نلزمك باعتراضك هذا تخطئة الله تعالى في تعليمه رسوله المبعوث صلى الله عليه وسلم لدعوة من اعتقد مع الله إلها آخر ودان بإثبات الشريك له دلائل الوحدانية واستحالة ألوهية من سواه من الأصنام والأوثان إذ ما علم من الدليل فاسد معترض لا دلالة فيه على ما استدل به عليه، إذ هو دليل عقلي ولا دلالة في العقل عليه، وليس في ثبوت العجز دلالة بطلان الألوهية فكان ما أثبته الله تعالى في القرآن وعلمه رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم من دلالة التوحيد وإبطال ألوهية من سواه ليحاج به من أعرض عنه وعانده فاسدا معترضا، ومن جوز على الله هذا فقد نسبه إلى الجهل والسفه لأنه تعالى إن لم يعلم بفساد هذا الدليل فهو جاهل، وإن علم بفساده، ومع ذلك علمه رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم ليحاج به من خالفه في التوحيد وتمسك بالشرك فهذا منه سفه ومن وصف الله تعالى بالجهل والسفه فقد كفر من ساعته ثم أبطل على نفسه الدلالة السمعية على إبطال القول بالتثنية والشرك، وذلك لأنه لما جاز عليه الجهل والسفه وجاز أيضا عليه العجز عما هو مقدور في نفسه وزوال قدرته عما تعلقت به قدرة غيره على ما قررنا في تعذر إثبات الوحدانية على أصلهم بما ذكرنا من الدليلين قبل دلالة التمانع لجاز عليه الكذب وتأييد الكذب بالدلائل، ولما لم يخرج بذلك عن الألوهية واستحقاق العبادة، لا يخرج عن ذلك بهذا أيضا، ولعله أقام جميع المعجزات على أيدي الكاذبين وفيه إبطال الدليل السمعي أصلا، ولا دلالة في العقل على إثبات الوحدانية عنده، فإذا لا دليل عليه من حيث العقل ولا من حيث السمع، ولعل مراد هذا الملحد، إبطال
[Abu Hashim and the proofs of unity and the refutation against him] When the turn of leadership of the Mu'tazila came to Abu Hashim, and he saw the impossibility of establishing unity by rational proofs according to their corrupt principles, and his predecessors were perplexed about that, he claimed that there is no rational indication (dalala) of the unity of the Maker (al-Sani'), and [said]: We know that the Maker is one by the indication of revelation (al-sam'), not by reason, and if we were left to our intellects we would deem it possible that the world has two or more makers. And he occupied himself with objecting to the proof of mutual prevention (dalalat al-tamānu'), which is the most famous proof of the people of tawhid. He claimed that their power or the power of one of them over what you [the upholders of tawhid] have mentioned would remove them or one of them from lordship, so this enters into the category of impossibilities which neither of them can be described as having power over nor as being incapable of, just as you have prohibited in the case of the One describing Him as having power over injustice, lying, and other attributes unbecoming to the Exalted and Majestic Creator, and [prohibited] describing Him as being incapable of them due to impossibility. Thus they make the same excuse regarding two [gods]. He said: We clarify it according to the statement of one who says that will is universal in existent things: that will, according to them, does not contradict what is known, and what is known does not contradict what exists, so how can one of them be imagined to have a will contrary to the will of the other, and in having a will contrary to the other there is a contradiction of what is known? It was said to him: The first thing we impose upon you by this objection of yours is charging God Almighty with error in His teaching of His sent Messenger (peace be upon him) for the call of one who believed in another god along with God and adhered to the affirmation of a partner for Him, [teaching him] the proofs of unity and the impossibility of the divinity of other than Him from idols and false gods, since what was taught of the proof is corrupt and objectionable, having no indication of what it was used as evidence for, because it is a rational proof and there is no rational indication of it, and the establishment of inability is not an indication of the invalidity of divinity. So what God established in the Quran and taught His Messenger (peace be upon him) of the proof of tawhid and the invalidation of the divinity of other than Him, to argue with it against one who turned away and opposed [him], becomes corrupt and objectionable. And whoever deems this permissible concerning God has attributed ignorance and folly to Him, because if He did not know the corruption of this proof, He is ignorant, and if He knew its corruption and still taught it to His Messenger (peace be upon him) to argue with it against those who opposed him in tawhid and adhered to shirk, then this is folly from Him. And whoever describes God as having ignorance and folly has disbelieved immediately. Then he nullified for himself the revealed indication of the invalidation of the statements of dualism and shirk, because when ignorance and folly are deemed possible for Him, also inability regarding what is possible in itself and the removal of His power over what the power of another is attached to, as we established in the impossibility of establishing unity according to their principle by the two proofs we mentioned before the proof of mutual prevention, then lying and the support of lying with proofs become possible for Him. And since He does not thereby leave divinity and the deservingness of worship, He does not leave that by this either. Perhaps He established all miracles at the hands of liars, and in that is the invalidation of the revealed proof entirely. And there is no rational indication of establishing unity according to him, so there is no proof of it from the standpoint of reason nor from the standpoint of revelation. And perhaps the intention of this heretic is to invalidate...
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a combined presentation and refutation of Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i's view that reason alone cannot prove the oneness of God. The author first sets the context: when Abu Hashim became the leader of the Mu'tazila, he saw that on their corrupt principles it was impossible to prove tawhid rationally, and his predecessors were confused. So he claimed that there is no rational proof for God's unity; we only know it from revelation. He then proceeded to object to the famous proof of mutual prevention (dalil al-tamānu'), which argues that if there were two gods, they would prevent each other from acting, leading to impossibility. Abu Hashim argued that even in the case of one God, certain actions (like injustice) are impossible not because of incapacity but because of their inherent unsuitability. Likewise, for two gods, the alleged mutual prevention is impossible not due to incapacity but due to the nature of the thing. He further clarified on the assumption of universal will that since will must align with what is known, two wills cannot contradict each other without contradiction in knowledge. The refutation begins with 'it was said to him': the first consequence of his objection is that it charges God with error. If the rational proof is invalid, then God either did not know it was invalid (ignorance) or knowingly taught an invalid proof (folly). Both are blasphemous. This accusation also undermines the revealed proof itself, because if God could be ignorant or foolish, then He could also be incapable, lie, and support lies with miracles. This destroys the reliability of revelation entirely. Since Abu Hashim denied rational proof and this refutation shows his position leads to invalidating revelation, he is left with no proof at all. The passage ends abruptly, suggesting that the author is exposing the heresy of those who reject rational arguments for tawhid.

Key Terms
أبو هاشم
دلالة التمانع
وحدانية الصانع
السمع
العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that rejecting rational proofs for tawhid is a neutral or humble position.
Correction: Abu Hashim's denial is not neutral; it challenges the very foundation of kalām and has far-reaching consequences, as the refutation will show.

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hashim, what is the source of knowledge for God's unity?
A) Reason alone
B) Revelation alone
C) Both reason and revelation
D) Mystical experience

Key Takeaway
Abu Hashim argued that rational proof cannot establish tawhid; only revelation can, and he objected to the proof of mutual prevention by comparing it to the impossibility of certain actions for one God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face doubts about God's oneness, do you instinctively reach for rational arguments or for the words of revelation? Which one actually settles your heart? If reason alone can't prove tawhid, as Abu Hashim claimed, does that make your faith more reliant on revelation—or does it unsettle you?
?
Abu Hashim argued that without revelation, we would deem multiple gods possible. Have you ever encountered a doubt that seemed logically plausible but clashed with what you know from scripture? How did you resolve it? Are you willing to let revelation be the final arbiter even when your reason resists?
?
The proof of mutual prevention is a sophisticated logical argument, but Abu Hashim rejected it by comparing it to the impossibility of God doing injustice. In your own life, do you sometimes rely on clever arguments to defend your faith while neglecting the direct authority of revelation? What would it cost you to submit entirely to what God has said, even if it feels intellectually unsatisfying?

Refuting Abu Hashim: Consequences of Denying Rational Proof
Refutation of Abu Hashim's position via reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refutation of Abu Hashim's position, which argues that denying rational proof leads to blasphemy and the destruction of revelation itself.

Core Idea
Denying rational proof forces God into ignorance or folly.

The refutation of Abu Hashim's denial begins with a powerful reductio ad absurdum. If rational proof of tawhid is invalid, then God either did not know it was invalid (ignorance) or knowingly taught an invalid proof (folly). Both attributions are blasphemous. Moreover, this argument undermines the very revelation that Abu Hashim claims to rely on, leaving no proof at all.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'قيل له' to the end. Focus on the logical steps of the argument.
The refutation is framed as a direct response to Abu Hashim.
2
Understand the first consequence
The refutation says that Abu Hashim's objection implies either God's ignorance (if He didn't know His proof was invalid) or His folly (if He knew it was invalid yet taught it).
These are considered blasphemous attributes.
3
Trace the collapse of revelation
The argument continues: if God can be ignorant or foolish, then He can also be incapable, lie, and support lies with miracles. This destroys the reliability of revelation entirely.
Abu Hashim relied on revelation, but this refutation shows his position makes revelation unreliable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[أبو هاشم ودلائل الوحدانية والرد عليه] فلما انتهت نوبة رئاسة المعتزلة إلى أبي هاشم ورأى تعذر إثبات الوحدانية بالدلائل العقلية على أصولهم الفاسدة وتحير سلفه في ذلك، فزعم أن لا دلالة في العقل على وحدانية الصانع، وإنا عرفنا أن الصانع واحد بدلالة السمع دون العقل، ولو خلينا وعقولنا لجوزنا أن يكون للعالم صانعان فأكثر واشتغل بالاعتراض على دلالة التمانع التي هي أشهر دلالات أهل التوحيد فزعم أن قدرتهما أو قدرة أحدهما على ما أوردتموه يخرجهما أو أحدهما عن الربوبية فدخل هذا في جملة المستحيلات التي لا يوصف أحدهما بالقدرة عليه ولا بالعجز عنه كما منعتموه في الواحد من الوصف بالقدرة على الظلم والكذب وسائر الأوصاف التي لا تليق بالباري عز وجل، ومن الوصف بالعجز عنها للاستحالة فكذا يعتذرون في الاثنين قال: ونوضحه على قول من يقول بتعميم الإرادة في الكائنات، أن الإرادة لا تخالف عندهم المعلوم، والمعلوم لا يخالف الكائن، فكيف يتوهم من أحدهما إرادة خلاف صاحبه وفي إرادة خلاف صاحبه خلاف معلومة، قيل له: إن أول ما نلزمك باعتراضك هذا تخطئة الله تعالى في تعليمه رسوله المبعوث صلى الله عليه وسلم لدعوة من اعتقد مع الله إلها آخر ودان بإثبات الشريك له دلائل الوحدانية واستحالة ألوهية من سواه من الأصنام والأوثان إذ ما علم من الدليل فاسد معترض لا دلالة فيه على ما استدل به عليه، إذ هو دليل عقلي ولا دلالة في العقل عليه، وليس في ثبوت العجز دلالة بطلان الألوهية فكان ما أثبته الله تعالى في القرآن وعلمه رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم من دلالة التوحيد وإبطال ألوهية من سواه ليحاج به من أعرض عنه وعانده فاسدا معترضا، ومن جوز على الله هذا فقد نسبه إلى الجهل والسفه لأنه تعالى إن لم يعلم بفساد هذا الدليل فهو جاهل، وإن علم بفساده، ومع ذلك علمه رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم ليحاج به من خالفه في التوحيد وتمسك بالشرك فهذا منه سفه ومن وصف الله تعالى بالجهل والسفه فقد كفر من ساعته ثم أبطل على نفسه الدلالة السمعية على إبطال القول بالتثنية والشرك، وذلك لأنه لما جاز عليه الجهل والسفه وجاز أيضا عليه العجز عما هو مقدور في نفسه وزوال قدرته عما تعلقت به قدرة غيره على ما قررنا في تعذر إثبات الوحدانية على أصلهم بما ذكرنا من الدليلين قبل دلالة التمانع لجاز عليه الكذب وتأييد الكذب بالدلائل، ولما لم يخرج بذلك عن الألوهية واستحقاق العبادة، لا يخرج عن ذلك بهذا أيضا، ولعله أقام جميع المعجزات على أيدي الكاذبين وفيه إبطال الدليل السمعي أصلا، ولا دلالة في العقل على إثبات الوحدانية عنده، فإذا لا دليل عليه من حيث العقل ولا من حيث السمع، ولعل مراد هذا الملحد، إبطال
[Abu Hashim and the proofs of unity and the refutation against him] When the turn of leadership of the Mu'tazila came to Abu Hashim, and he saw the impossibility of establishing unity by rational proofs according to their corrupt principles, and his predecessors were perplexed about that, he claimed that there is no rational indication (dalala) of the unity of the Maker (al-Sani'), and [said]: We know that the Maker is one by the indication of revelation (al-sam'), not by reason, and if we were left to our intellects we would deem it possible that the world has two or more makers. And he occupied himself with objecting to the proof of mutual prevention (dalalat al-tamānu'), which is the most famous proof of the people of tawhid. He claimed that their power or the power of one of them over what you [the upholders of tawhid] have mentioned would remove them or one of them from lordship, so this enters into the category of impossibilities which neither of them can be described as having power over nor as being incapable of, just as you have prohibited in the case of the One describing Him as having power over injustice, lying, and other attributes unbecoming to the Exalted and Majestic Creator, and [prohibited] describing Him as being incapable of them due to impossibility. Thus they make the same excuse regarding two [gods]. He said: We clarify it according to the statement of one who says that will is universal in existent things: that will, according to them, does not contradict what is known, and what is known does not contradict what exists, so how can one of them be imagined to have a will contrary to the will of the other, and in having a will contrary to the other there is a contradiction of what is known? It was said to him: The first thing we impose upon you by this objection of yours is charging God Almighty with error in His teaching of His sent Messenger (peace be upon him) for the call of one who believed in another god along with God and adhered to the affirmation of a partner for Him, [teaching him] the proofs of unity and the impossibility of the divinity of other than Him from idols and false gods, since what was taught of the proof is corrupt and objectionable, having no indication of what it was used as evidence for, because it is a rational proof and there is no rational indication of it, and the establishment of inability is not an indication of the invalidity of divinity. So what God established in the Quran and taught His Messenger (peace be upon him) of the proof of tawhid and the invalidation of the divinity of other than Him, to argue with it against one who turned away and opposed [him], becomes corrupt and objectionable. And whoever deems this permissible concerning God has attributed ignorance and folly to Him, because if He did not know the corruption of this proof, He is ignorant, and if He knew its corruption and still taught it to His Messenger (peace be upon him) to argue with it against those who opposed him in tawhid and adhered to shirk, then this is folly from Him. And whoever describes God as having ignorance and folly has disbelieved immediately. Then he nullified for himself the revealed indication of the invalidation of the statements of dualism and shirk, because when ignorance and folly are deemed possible for Him, also inability regarding what is possible in itself and the removal of His power over what the power of another is attached to, as we established in the impossibility of establishing unity according to their principle by the two proofs we mentioned before the proof of mutual prevention, then lying and the support of lying with proofs become possible for Him. And since He does not thereby leave divinity and the deservingness of worship, He does not leave that by this either. Perhaps He established all miracles at the hands of liars, and in that is the invalidation of the revealed proof entirely. And there is no rational indication of establishing unity according to him, so there is no proof of it from the standpoint of reason nor from the standpoint of revelation. And perhaps the intention of this heretic is to invalidate...
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a combined presentation and refutation of Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i's view that reason alone cannot prove the oneness of God. The author first sets the context: when Abu Hashim became the leader of the Mu'tazila, he saw that on their corrupt principles it was impossible to prove tawhid rationally, and his predecessors were confused. So he claimed that there is no rational proof for God's unity; we only know it from revelation. He then proceeded to object to the famous proof of mutual prevention (dalil al-tamānu'), which argues that if there were two gods, they would prevent each other from acting, leading to impossibility. Abu Hashim argued that even in the case of one God, certain actions (like injustice) are impossible not because of incapacity but because of their inherent unsuitability. Likewise, for two gods, the alleged mutual prevention is impossible not due to incapacity but due to the nature of the thing. He further clarified on the assumption of universal will that since will must align with what is known, two wills cannot contradict each other without contradiction in knowledge. The refutation begins with 'it was said to him': the first consequence of his objection is that it charges God with error. If the rational proof is invalid, then God either did not know it was invalid (ignorance) or knowingly taught an invalid proof (folly). Both are blasphemous. This accusation also undermines the revealed proof itself, because if God could be ignorant or foolish, then He could also be incapable, lie, and support lies with miracles. This destroys the reliability of revelation entirely. Since Abu Hashim denied rational proof and this refutation shows his position leads to invalidating revelation, he is left with no proof at all. The passage ends abruptly, suggesting that the author is exposing the heresy of those who reject rational arguments for tawhid.

Key Terms
الجهل
السفه
السمع
الدليل العقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that rejecting rational proofs for God's unity is a safe, fideistic position.
Correction: This refutation shows that such a position necessarily attributes ignorance or folly to God and destroys the reliability of revelation.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, what does Abu Hashim's objection imply about God?
A) That God is all-powerful
B) That God is ignorant or foolish
C) That God is merciful
D) That God is just

Key Takeaway
The refutation of Abu Hashim demonstrates that denying rational proof for tawhid leads to attributing ignorance or folly to God and ultimately invalidates revelation itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a theological question that seems too complex, do you ever find yourself wishing you could simply avoid rational reasoning altogether? This lesson warns that such avoidance can lead to attributing ignorance to God. How will you commit to embracing both reason and revelation in your faith, even when it is difficult?
?
The argument here shows that a seemingly small objection can lead to devastating consequences for one's entire worldview. Are there any beliefs or practices in your life that you have not fully thought through, perhaps because their logical conclusions might be uncomfortable? Will you now trace those consequences to ensure you are not unknowingly holding views unworthy of God?
?
Consider the seriousness of attributing ignorance or folly to God—even indirectly through a theological position you hold. Have you ever held a view that, if pushed to its logical end, would imply something unbefitting of God? Are you willing to lay that view before God and ask for guidance to correct it, no matter how attached you are to it?

The Danger of Rejecting Prophethood and Laws
The author refutes an opponent who denies prophethood and laws, accusing them of hypocrisy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how denying prophethood and divine laws leads to the rejection of tawhid, and why such an opponent's claim to be 'People of Justice and Oneness' is hypocritical.

Core Idea
Rejecting prophethood and laws ultimately destroys the foundation of tawhid.

The author begins by exposing the real consequence of denying prophethood and Sharia: it unravels the entire religion, especially the core belief in God's oneness. He then expresses astonishment that such an opponent still dares to call themselves 'People of Justice and Oneness'—a blatant contradiction that reveals their shamelessness. This lesson examines that accusation and the author's lament over those who follow such misguided leaders.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the author's tone of shock and condemnation.
The author uses strong language to highlight the gravity of the opponent's error.
2
Identify the opponent's position
The opponent denies prophethood and religious laws. Understand why the author says this leads to corrupting tawhid.
The author links rejection of laws to abandonment of tawhid ('إفضائها إلى إبطال القول بالوحدانية').
3
Examine the hypocrisy charge
The opponent claims the title 'Ahl al-‘Adl wa al-Tawhid' (People of Justice and Oneness). The author finds this outrageous given his actual beliefs.
This title was commonly used by the Mu‘tazila, whom the author is likely refuting.
4
Reflect on the followers
The author is amazed that anyone would follow such an obviously corrupt opinion. Consider why people might follow even false leaders.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوحدانية وإفساد القول بالرسالة، ودفع الشرائع بأسرها وهدم قواعد الدين عن أصلها، ولولا هذا لكان إذا بَان له فساد مذهب القدرية، لإفضائها إلى إبطال القول بالوحدانية لتركها، وأخذ بمذاهب أهل الحق ولما صار إلى تقوية القول بالتثنية، وإبطال دلائل التوحيد وحيث لم ينقد للحق ولم يقر ببطلان ما كان عليه من المذاهب دل على أن مراده ما ذكرنا ثم العجب أنه مع هذه العقيدة يلقب نفسه أهل العدل والتوحيد، وهذا هو آية الوقاحة وقلة الحياء والدين، وأعجب من هذا كله أنه لم يعدم من يتبعه على هذا الرأي البادي عواره والظاهر فساده الهادم لقواعد الدين المؤيد لأقاويل الملحدين، ويرضى به إماما يعتمد عليه ويلقي مقاليد أمور دينه إليه. والله تعالى يعصمنا عن قول يفضي إلى الإلحاد، ويصوننا من الزيغ عن سبيل الرشاد ثم يقال له: أليس أن الله قال : لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَتَا وقال عز وجل : وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُ مِنْ إِلَهِ إِذًا لَذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِلَهِ بِمَا خَلَقَ وما ذكر من الآيات التي مر ذكرها، ولا شك أن علو البعض على البعض وفساد السماوات والأرض غير متصور مع الاتفاق في الإرادة فلو كان الاختلاف فيها غير متصور لكان الله تعالى معلما رسوله لولا أن يحاج المشركين بما لا يصلح أن يكون دليلا، وكذا بتعليمه إياه محاجة الكفرة بالدليل العقلي، مع أنه لا دلالة فيه على ذلك كان سفيها جاهلا، ومن نسب الله تعالى إلى شيء من ذلك كان ممن لا يخفى كفره على أحد، ولوجب على أقرب الناس إليه إبانة رأسه عن جسده وقطع مادة شره عن ضعفاء المسلمين.
Oneness [of God] and corrupting the statement on prophethood, and repelling all religious laws and demolishing the foundations of religion from its root. If it were not for this, then when the corruption of the Qadariyya school became clear to him—because it leads to the negation of the statement on oneness by abandoning it—he would have adopted the schools of the people of truth and would not have proceeded to strengthen the statement on duality and invalidate the proofs of tawhid. Since he did not submit to the truth and did not acknowledge the falsehood of the schools he held, this indicates that his intention is what we mentioned. Then astonishingly, with this creed, he labels himself 'People of Justice and Oneness,' and this is the epitome of shamelessness, lack of modesty, and lack of religion. Even more astonishing than all this is that he does not lack followers who adhere to this opinion—whose defects are apparent and whose corruption is evident, which demolishes the foundations of religion and supports the sayings of the heretics—and they accept him as a reliable imam and entrust the reins of their religious affairs to him. May Allah Almighty protect us from a statement that leads to heresy, and guard us from deviating from the path of guidance. Then it is said to him: Is it not that Allah said: 'If there were gods in them besides Allah, they would have corrupted' and He, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'And there was no god with Him; otherwise each god would have gone off with what he created'? There is no doubt that the superiority of some over others and the corruption of the heavens and earth are inconceivable with agreement in will. If disagreement in them were inconceivable, then Allah Almighty would have taught His messenger, otherwise he would argue with the polytheists using something that is not suitable as a proof. Likewise, teaching him to argue with the disbelievers using an intellectual proof, while there is no indication in it of that, would make Him foolish and ignorant. Whoever attributes anything of that to Allah Almighty is one whose disbelief is not hidden from anyone, and it would be incumbent on those closest to him to separate his head from his body and cut off the source of his evil from the weak Muslims.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a polemical refutation of an unnamed opponent who rejects prophethood and divine laws. The author argues that this rejection leads to the denial of divine oneness (tawhid) and ultimately to polytheism. He expresses astonishment that this opponent, despite his beliefs, claims the title 'People of Justice and Oneness' (أهل العدل والتوحيد), a common self-designation of the Mu'tazila. The author calls this shamelessness and notes that the opponent still finds followers. The author then invokes Quranic verses (Surah al-Anbiya 22 and Surah al-Mu'minun 91) as proof that multiple gods would lead to corruption and separation. He argues that if the Quranic proof were invalid, it would imply that Allah taught His messenger a flawed argument, which would be foolishness—an impossible attribution to Allah. Thus, anyone who claims such is a disbeliever deserving of execution by the ruler.

الرسالة
الشرائع
التوحيد
القدرية

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that denying only prophethood and laws does not affect belief in God's oneness.
Correction: The author argues that rejecting divine laws leads to abandoning the proof of tawhid, ultimately resulting in polytheism.

Checkpoint
What does the author claim is the ultimate consequence of the opponent's rejection of prophethood and laws?
A) Strengthening of tawhid
B) Denial of divine oneness and polytheism
C) Acceptance of Qadariyya
D) Justice and fairness

Key Takeaway
Denying prophethood and divine laws is not a separate issue—it directly undermines the belief in God's oneness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly submit to all of Allah's laws sent through the prophets, or do you selectively choose parts that fit your desires while claiming to believe in tawhid? What would the author say about your consistency?
?
Whom do you trust as an imam or religious guide? Have you examined whether their teachings preserve the foundations of religion or, as the author warns, inadvertently support heresy?
?
The author prays for protection from heretical speech. When was the last time you spoke about religion without knowledge or carelessly repeated a doubt? Will you commit to guarding your tongue as an act of preserving tawhid?

Sects and Disagreements

Quranic Proof of Tawhid and the Consequence of Denial
The author uses Quranic verses to prove tawhid and argues that denying them implies kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quranic verses (21:22 and 23:91) prove tawhid, and why rejecting these proofs would imply an impossibility—that Allah taught His Prophet a flawed argument—which constitutes kufr.

Core Idea
The Quran itself provides clear proof that multiple gods would lead to corruption; to deny its validity is to accuse Allah of foolishness.

After condemning the opponent's rejection of prophethood, the author now mounts a rational argument from the Quran. He cites two verses that show the logical impossibility of multiple gods—if there were more than one, the universe would fall into chaos. He then makes a startling point: if this Quranic argument were invalid, it would mean Allah taught His Prophet a defective proof, which is absurd and blasphemous. This lesson unpacks that argument and its severe conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses cited
Read the Arabic verses: 'لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَتَا' (21:22) and 'وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُ مِنْ إِلَهِ إِذًا لَذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِلَهِ بِمَا خَلَقَ' (23:91). Understand their plain meaning.
The verses are used as proof that multiple gods lead to conflict and corruption.
2
Understand the author's argument
The author argues that if multiple gods existed, they would either agree or disagree. Disagreement causes corruption, but agreement is impossible because each would have independent will.
The author rejects the possibility of 'agreement in will' as inconceivable for multiple independent gods.
3
Consider the hypothetical objection
The author anticipates an objection: what if the Quranic proof is invalid? He then shows that accepting that would force us to say Allah taught His Prophet a flawed argument, which is impossible and blasphemous.
This is a reductio ad absurdum: denying the proof leads to kufr.
4
Reflect on the final consequence
The author concludes that anyone who attributes such a flaw to Allah is a disbeliever deserving capital punishment.
The strong language reflects the seriousness of the accusation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quranic proof that multiple gods would lead to corruption, do you fully accept it in your heart, or have you ever entertained subtle doubts about the oneness of Allah? If so, what would it mean for your faith if you rejected even one clear proof?
?
The passage says that attributing foolishness to Allah is obvious disbelief. Have you ever spoken or thought about Allah in a way that unintentionally diminished His perfect wisdom? How can you train your tongue and heart to avoid such slips?
?
If someone you love—a family member or close friend—denied a clear Quranic proof of tawhid, would you have the courage to confront them as the passage suggests? What holds you back from speaking the truth, even when it is difficult?

The Magian Claim of Two Creators and Its Refutation
The author states the Magian dualist claim and refutes it by the proven oneness of the Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Magian dualist belief in Yazdan and Ahriman and why it is invalidated by the oneness of the Creator.

Core Idea
The Magians' two-creator theory collapses once you affirm one eternal Creator.

Before diving into the internal disagreements among the Magians, we first need to see the core of their belief: two creators, one good and one evil. The author begins this passage by stating that the unity of the Creator has already been proven, and therefore the Magian claim is false. He then outlines their view to show its inconsistency.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get the flow. Notice the names Yazdan and Ahriman.
The footnote markers (۲), (۴), (۳) are editorial.
2
Identify the two creators
Find where the author describes what each creator produces. Yazdan creates good, Ahriman creates evil and harmful things.
3
Understand the refutation
The author says 'if it is established that the ancient Creator is one, the statement of the Magians is invalidated.' This is the core refutation.
The refutation is brief; the author assumes the proof of oneness is already given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲ – [الكلام في إبطال قول المجوس(۲)]: بزدان وأهر من عند المجوس]: صانعين: أحدهما (٤) خیر ثم (۳) إذا ثبت بما بينا أن الصانع القديم واحد ، بطل قول المجوس: إن للعالم خلق ما كان من أجزاء العالم حسنا ويسمى عندهم يزدان والآخر شرير كل شر وفساد في العالم منه، وهو الذي خلق الأجسام الضارة، والسموم القاتلة، والأجساد المستقذرة المنتنة، ويسمى عندهم أهرمن، واتفقوا على أنه القول بقدم يزدان، واختلفوا في أهر من زعم بعضهم أنه قديم، وزعم بعضهم حدث من فكرة ردية حصلت من يزدان، فإنه تفكر في نفسه هل يخرج عليه من يضاده في ملكه، فتولد من هذه الفكرة عفونة في بعضه، وتولد من تلك العفونة أهرمن، وقالت فرقة منهم يسمون المسخية : إن يزدان (٥) كان نورا محضا ثم انمسخ بعضه فصار ظلمة، فكان أهر من من تلك الظلمة ، وقوم منهم يقال لهم الزروانية (٦)، يزعمون أن زروان وهو النور القديم عندهم شك في صلاته شكة فحدث الشيطان وهو أهر من من تلك الشكة، وإنما كان يصلي طلبا أن يكون له ولد. وبعضهم قالوا: لا بل زمزم زروان في صلاته سبعة آلاف سنة وتسعمائة وتسعا وتسعين سنة
2 – [Discussion on the Abrogation of the Magians' Statement]: [Yazdan and Ahriman according to the Magians]: Two creators: one of them good. Then, when it is established by what we have made clear that the ancient Creator is one, the statement of the Magians is invalidated: that for the world there is a creator who created what is good from the parts of the world, called by them Yazdan, and another evil, every evil and corruption in the world is from him, and he is the one who created harmful bodies, lethal poisons, and foul disgusting bodies, and he is called by them Ahriman. And they agreed on the claim of the eternity of Yazdan, and they disagreed about Ahriman: some claimed that he is eternal, and some claimed that he originated from a bad thought that occurred from Yazdan. For he (Yazdan) reflected in himself whether there would arise against him one who opposes him in his kingdom, so from this reflection a putrefaction was generated in some of him, and from that putrefaction Ahriman originated. And a group of them called al-Maskhiyya said: Yazdan was pure light, then some of it transformed and became darkness, so Ahriman was from that darkness. And a people among them called al-Zarwaniyya claim that Zarwan, which is the ancient light according to them, doubted in his prayer a doubt, so Satan (i.e., Ahriman) originated from that doubt, and he was only praying seeking to have a child. And some of them said: No, rather Zarwan hummed in his prayer for seven thousand, nine hundred and ninety-nine years.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the dualist belief of the Magians (al-Majūs). After having proven the oneness of the ancient Creator (al-Ṣāniʿ al-Qadīm), the author states that the Magian claim of two creators is invalidated. He explains their view: one creator, Yazdan, produces all good in the world; the other, Ahriman, produces all evil—harmful bodies, poisons, filth. They agree that Yazdan is eternal, but disagree about Ahriman. Some say Ahriman is also eternal; others say he originated from a bad thought that occurred to Yazdan. The author then describes the process: Yazdan reflected on whether an opponent would arise, a putrefaction formed from that thought, and from it Ahriman emerged. Another sect, al-Maskhiyya, holds that Yazdan was pure light, then part of it transformed into darkness, becoming Ahriman. Another sect, al-Zarwaniyya, claims that Zarwan (the ancient light) doubted during his prayer, and from that doubt came the devil (Ahriman); Zarwan was praying to have a child. Yet others say Zarwan hummed in prayer for nearly ten thousand years. The author presents these differing accounts to show the inconsistency of Magian doctrine, reinforcing that only belief in one Creator is coherent.

Key Terms
مجوس (Majūs)
يزدان (Yazdan)
أهرمن (Ahriman)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Belief in two creators is a coherent alternative to monotheism.
Correction: The author shows that the Magians cannot even agree on the nature of the second creator, Ahriman, which demonstrates the incoherence of their position.

Checkpoint
According to the Magians as described in the passage, what does Yazdan create?
A) Everything in the world
B) All that is good and beautiful in the world
C) Only harmful things
D) Nothing; he is inactive

Key Takeaway
The Magian belief in two creators is invalidated by the oneness of the divine essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial or see evil in the world, does your heart ever whisper that there must be a power opposing God? How can you reaffirm your tawhid in that moment?
?
The Magians created a separate deity to explain evil rather than submitting to the one Creator's absolute sovereignty. Is there any area of your life where you are tempted to 'excuse' God's control by attributing things to chance, other people, or 'bad luck'?
?
If you truly believe that the one Creator is in control of both good and evil, how must you change the way you respond to suffering? Write down one concrete step you will take this week to act on that belief.

Internal Disagreements Among the Magians About Ahriman's Origin
The author presents three divergent Magian accounts of Ahriman's origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will learn the three different Magian accounts of how Ahriman came into existence and how these contradictions undermine their dualism.

Core Idea
The Magians cannot even agree on where evil came from.

Having established that the Magians claim two creators, the author now exposes their deep internal disagreements. He reports three different stories about Ahriman's origin, each more fantastic than the last. These contradictions show that their doctrine is not based on sound reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the detailed disagreements
Read the Arabic passage that describes the various opinions. Notice the different sects mentioned: al-Maskhiyya and al-Zarwaniyya.
2
List the four views
Identify each view: some say Ahriman is eternal, some say he originated from a bad thought, some from transformation of light, some from doubt in prayer.
The view that Ahriman is eternal is mentioned first.
3
Reflect on the contradictions
Consider that these conflicting origin stories show the Magians could not agree on a consistent doctrine. This reinforces the author's refutation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that the Magians could not agree on where evil came from. Where do you turn when you face doubts about the origin of evil in your own life? Are you searching for answers in contradictory sources, or have you submitted fully to the clear truth of tawheed? What one step can you take today to strengthen your certainty that Allah alone is the Creator of all, both good and evil?
?
The Magians invented multiple stories about Ahriman because they tried to explain evil apart from the oneness of God. Examine your own heart: do you ever attribute the evil you experience to sources other than the decree of Allah? How might that lead you away from complete reliance on Him? Write down one specific situation where you must remind yourself that everything comes from Allah.
?
Zarwaniyya claimed that even their god Zarwan doubted. If you are honest, do you sometimes have doubts about Allah's wisdom or justice because of the evil you see? This lesson exposes the confusion of those who set up partners with Allah. Are you willing to bring those doubts directly to Allah in sincere prayer and ask Him for clarity, rather than entertaining false alternatives? What will you do the next time such a doubt crosses your mind?

The Magian Claim of Two Creators
Nasafi states the Magian belief in two creators and their agreement on Yezdan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core Magian dualist belief as presented by Nasafi and the key point of agreement among them that Yezdan is eternal.

Core Idea
The Magians agree on one eternal creator but disagree on the origin of the other.

Nasafi begins his refutation by first presenting the Magian claim that there are two creators, one good and one evil. He then notes that all Magians agree that Yezdan, the good creator, is eternal. This sets up the inconsistency and internal disagreements among the Magians themselves, which Nasafi will later detail.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze. Then read the translation. Notice the contrast between the two creators and the agreement on Yezdan.
The passage begins by referencing a previous proof of God's oneness.
2
Identify the two creators
Find the names and attributes of the two creators: Yezdan (good, light, etc.) and Ahriman (evil, source of corruption).
3
Observe the agreement and disagreement
Notice that all Magians agree that Yezdan is eternal, but they differ on Ahriman. This internal division is a key point in Nasafi's refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إذا ثبت بما بينا أن الصانع القديم واحد، بطل قول المجوس: إن للعالم صانعين: أحدهما خير ويسمى عندهم يزدان والآخر شرير كل شر وفساد في العالم منه، وهو الذي خلق الأجسام الضارة، والسموم القاتلة، والأجساد المستقذرة المنتنة، ويسمى عندهم أهرمن، واتفقوا على أن القول بقدم يزدان، واختلفوا في أهرمن: زعم بعضهم أنه قديم، وزعم بعضهم أنه حدث من فكرة ردية حصلت من يزدان، فإنه تفكر في نفسه هل يخرج عليه من يضاده في ملكه، فتولد من هذه الفكرة عفونة في بعضه، وتولد من تلك العفونة أهرمن، وقالت فرقة منهم يسمون المسخية: إن يزدان كان نورا محضا ثم انمسخ بعضه فصار ظلمة، فكان أهرمن من تلك الظلمة، وقوم منهم يقال لهم الزروانية، يزعمون أن زروان وهو النور القديم عندهم شك في صلاته شكة فحدث الشيطان وهو أهرمن من تلك الشكة، وإنما كان يصلي طلبا أن يكون له ولد. وبعضهم قالوا: لا بل زمزم زروان في صلاته سبعة آلاف سنة وتسعمائة وتسعا وتسعين سنة ليكون له ابن ثم اهتم وقال لعل هذا لا يكون فكان أهرمن من العلم الأول، وإبليس وهو عندهم أهرمن من هذا الهم ثم هم مع اختلافهم زعموا أن أهرمن حارب يزدان ودامت المحاربة بينهما ثلاثة آلاف سنة، ثم وقعت بينهما هدنة، فهما على تلك الهدنة إلى أن تنقضي مدة الهدنة، ولهم في بدء الخلق خرافات كثيرة، لا يطيق العقل إحضارها على القلب لركاكتها في نفسها.
Then, when it has been established by what we have shown that the Maker, the Eternal, is One, the saying of the Magians is invalidated: that the world has two makers: one good, called by them Yezdan, and the other evil, every evil and corruption in the world from him, and he is the one who created harmful bodies, deadly poisons, and foul, stinking corpses, and he is called by them Ahriman. And they agreed on the eternity of Yezdan, but differed concerning Ahriman: some claimed he is eternal, some claimed he originated from a bad thought that came from Yezdan, for he reflected in himself whether someone would come out against him in his kingdom, so from this thought a corruption arose in some of him, and from that corruption Ahriman was generated. And a sect of them called al-Masikhiyya said: Yezdan was pure light, then some of him transformed into darkness, so Ahriman came from that darkness. And a people called al-Zarwaniyya claim that Zarwan, who is the eternal light according to them, doubted in his prayer with a doubt, so Satan, who is Ahriman, came from that doubt; and he was only praying seeking to have a son. And some said: No, rather Zarwan muttered in his prayer for seven thousand nine hundred and ninety-nine years to have a son, then he became anxious and said: Perhaps this will not happen, so Ahriman came from the first knowledge, and Iblis, who according to them is Ahriman, came from this anxiety. Then, despite their differences, they claimed that Ahriman fought Yezdan, and the war between them lasted three thousand years, then a truce occurred between them, and they remain on that truce until the truce period ends. And they have many fables concerning the beginning of creation, which the mind cannot bring to the heart due to their absurdity.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents the refutation of Magian dualism by first invoking the previously established proof of the oneness of the eternal Maker, then describing the Magian beliefs in two creators and their various contradictory myths. The author begins by stating that since it has been proven that the Creator is One, the Magian claim of two creators is invalidated. He then details their belief: one creator, Yezdan, is good; the other, Ahriman, is evil and the source of all harm and corruption. The Magians agree that Yezdan is eternal, but they differ on Ahriman. Some say Ahriman is eternal; others claim he originated from a bad thought in Yezdan's mind, generating corruption. Another group, al-Masikhiyya, says Yezdan was pure light that partially transformed into darkness, producing Ahriman. The Zarwaniyya claim that Zarwan, the eternal light, doubted in his prayer, producing Ahriman. Others give a detailed story of Zarwan's muttering and anxiety, leading to Ahriman's appearance from the 'first knowledge' and 'anxiety'. The Magians also claim a war and truce between Yezdan and Ahriman. The author concludes by noting the many absurd fables about the beginning of creation that the mind cannot accept due to their ridiculousness.

Key Terms
المجوس
يزدان
أهرمن
قديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Magian dualist belief is a coherent, unified theology.
Correction: Nasafi shows that even within Magianism, there is disagreement on the origin of Ahriman, undermining its coherence.

Checkpoint
According to the Magians as described, what do all of them agree upon regarding Yezdan?
A) He is eternal
B) He is created
C) He is evil
D) He doubted

Key Takeaway
The Magians agree that Yezdan is eternal, but their dualism creates internal contradictions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you have any beliefs about Allah that contradict each other, similar to how the Magians agreed on Yezdan's eternity but differed on Ahriman? How can you ensure your beliefs are consistent with the oneness of Allah?
?
When you face evil or hardship, do you ever subconsciously think of it as coming from a source other than Allah, as if there were two powers? What does this lesson teach you about where evil truly comes from?
?
Is there any area of your life where you act as if good comes from Allah but evil comes from somewhere else? How would embracing the complete oneness of Allah change your response to difficulties?

Magian Myths on Ahriman's Origin and the War
Nasafi enumerates the differing Magian beliefs on Ahriman's origin and recounts their war myth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different Magian sects' explanations for the origin of Ahriman and their myth of a battle and truce.

Core Idea
Magian myths about Ahriman's origin are contradictory and absurd.

Nasafi details various conflicting accounts of how Ahriman came to be. Some say he is eternal, others say he came from a bad thought, transformation, doubt, or anxiety. Nasafi then narrates the myth of a war and truce between the two creators, concluding that these are fables too absurd for reason.

Guided Path
1
Identify the different views on Ahriman's origin
Read the passage and list the various explanations given by the Magian sects: eternal, from a bad thought, transformation, doubt, etc.
Note the names of the sects: Masikhiyya, Zarwaniyya.
2
Recognize the internal conflicts
Observe how these accounts contradict each other. This is a key part of Nasafi's refutation.
3
Reflect on the war and truce myth
Consider why Nasafi presents this story and how it reinforces the absurdity of Magian beliefs.
Think about the logical implications of a war between two eternal beings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إذا ثبت بما بينا أن الصانع القديم واحد، بطل قول المجوس: إن للعالم صانعين: أحدهما خير ويسمى عندهم يزدان والآخر شرير كل شر وفساد في العالم منه، وهو الذي خلق الأجسام الضارة، والسموم القاتلة، والأجساد المستقذرة المنتنة، ويسمى عندهم أهرمن، واتفقوا على أن القول بقدم يزدان، واختلفوا في أهرمن: زعم بعضهم أنه قديم، وزعم بعضهم أنه حدث من فكرة ردية حصلت من يزدان، فإنه تفكر في نفسه هل يخرج عليه من يضاده في ملكه، فتولد من هذه الفكرة عفونة في بعضه، وتولد من تلك العفونة أهرمن، وقالت فرقة منهم يسمون المسخية: إن يزدان كان نورا محضا ثم انمسخ بعضه فصار ظلمة، فكان أهرمن من تلك الظلمة، وقوم منهم يقال لهم الزروانية، يزعمون أن زروان وهو النور القديم عندهم شك في صلاته شكة فحدث الشيطان وهو أهرمن من تلك الشكة، وإنما كان يصلي طلبا أن يكون له ولد. وبعضهم قالوا: لا بل زمزم زروان في صلاته سبعة آلاف سنة وتسعمائة وتسعا وتسعين سنة ليكون له ابن ثم اهتم وقال لعل هذا لا يكون فكان أهرمن من العلم الأول، وإبليس وهو عندهم أهرمن من هذا الهم ثم هم مع اختلافهم زعموا أن أهرمن حارب يزدان ودامت المحاربة بينهما ثلاثة آلاف سنة، ثم وقعت بينهما هدنة، فهما على تلك الهدنة إلى أن تنقضي مدة الهدنة، ولهم في بدء الخلق خرافات كثيرة، لا يطيق العقل إحضارها على القلب لركاكتها في نفسها.
Then, when it has been established by what we have shown that the Maker, the Eternal, is One, the saying of the Magians is invalidated: that the world has two makers: one good, called by them Yezdan, and the other evil, every evil and corruption in the world from him, and he is the one who created harmful bodies, deadly poisons, and foul, stinking corpses, and he is called by them Ahriman. And they agreed on the eternity of Yezdan, but differed concerning Ahriman: some claimed he is eternal, some claimed he originated from a bad thought that came from Yezdan, for he reflected in himself whether someone would come out against him in his kingdom, so from this thought a corruption arose in some of him, and from that corruption Ahriman was generated. And a sect of them called al-Masikhiyya said: Yezdan was pure light, then some of him transformed into darkness, so Ahriman came from that darkness. And a people called al-Zarwaniyya claim that Zarwan, who is the eternal light according to them, doubted in his prayer with a doubt, so Satan, who is Ahriman, came from that doubt; and he was only praying seeking to have a son. And some said: No, rather Zarwan muttered in his prayer for seven thousand nine hundred and ninety-nine years to have a son, then he became anxious and said: Perhaps this will not happen, so Ahriman came from the first knowledge, and Iblis, who according to them is Ahriman, came from this anxiety. Then, despite their differences, they claimed that Ahriman fought Yezdan, and the war between them lasted three thousand years, then a truce occurred between them, and they remain on that truce until the truce period ends. And they have many fables concerning the beginning of creation, which the mind cannot bring to the heart due to their absurdity.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents the refutation of Magian dualism by first invoking the previously established proof of the oneness of the eternal Maker, then describing the Magian beliefs in two creators and their various contradictory myths. The author begins by stating that since it has been proven that the Creator is One, the Magian claim of two creators is invalidated. He then details their belief: one creator, Yezdan, is good; the other, Ahriman, is evil and the source of all harm and corruption. The Magians agree that Yezdan is eternal, but they differ on Ahriman. Some say Ahriman is eternal; others claim he originated from a bad thought in Yezdan's mind, generating corruption. Another group, al-Masikhiyya, says Yezdan was pure light that partially transformed into darkness, producing Ahriman. The Zarwaniyya claim that Zarwan, the eternal light, doubted in his prayer, producing Ahriman. Others give a detailed story of Zarwan's muttering and anxiety, leading to Ahriman's appearance from the 'first knowledge' and 'anxiety'. The Magians also claim a war and truce between Yezdan and Ahriman. The author concludes by noting the many absurd fables about the beginning of creation that the mind cannot accept due to their ridiculousness.

Misconception: The Magians had a unified, consistent theology about the origin of evil.
Correction: Nasafi shows multiple contradictory accounts, revealing that Magian beliefs are inconsistent and irrational.

The Magian myths are internally contradictory and rationally absurd, undermining their dualist claim.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Magians invented elaborate myths to explain the existence of evil. Where in your own life have you allowed your reasoning or imagination to form ideas about Allah that are not grounded in the Qur'an and Sunna? Will you commit to testing every belief you hold about Allah against revelation, even if it feels uncomfortable?
?
Were you tempted to dismiss the Magian myths as 'absurd' while failing to see the subtle ways you might rationalize away the clear teachings of tawheed? What would it mean for you to submit totally to Allah's oneness, without allowing any mental reservations or invented explanations about good and evil?
?
Imagine you are standing before Allah and He asks you: 'Did you accept My oneness as I revealed it, or did you mix it with your own thoughts and cultural stories?' Right now, can you identify one belief or habit that compromises your tawheed? What is one concrete step you will take today to purify it?
