The Magian Doubt: Evil and the Need for a Second Creator
Magian argument for duality from the existence of evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Magian argument for the duality of creators based on the existence of evil, and its challenge to Islamic monotheism.

Core Idea
The Magians argue that evil proves a separate creator because a wise God cannot create evil.

Islamic theologians engaged with many pre-Islamic religions. The Magian (Zoroastrian) argument for two creators—one good, one evil—is a classic challenge that requires careful response. In this passage, the author presents their doubt, which will later be refuted.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the argument moves from observed evil to a necessary conclusion.
2
Identify the premises
Find the premises of the Magian argument: the existence of harmful things, the wisdom of God, and the impossibility of foolishness for Him.
3
Trace the inference to a second creator
Observe how they conclude that evil must have a foolish originator (Ahriman), and that the creator of evil is evil.
The conclusion is that evil was created by another, not by God.
4
Reflect on the theological challenge
Consider why this argument is a serious challenge to the belief in one all-powerful, all-good God.
Think about how an Islamic theologian might respond.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة المجوس في إثنينيية الخالق: وشبهتهم أن من أجزاء العالم ما هو ضار قبيح مستقذر، وإيجاد هذه الأشياء ليس بحكمه، والباري حكيم فلن يجوز منه إيجاد هذه الأشياء، لما أنه يستحيل عليه السفه ولا شك أنها محدثة، فلابد لها من محدث، فعلمنا أن لها محدثا سفيها وهو أهر من، وكذا موجد الشر شرير والباري جل وعلا منزه عن هذا الوصف، فدل أن وجود الشر كان بإيجاد غيره لا بإيجاده.
The doubt of the Magians about the duality of the Creator: Their doubt is that among the parts of the world there is that which is harmful, ugly, and disgusting, and the creation of these things is not in accordance with wisdom, and the Creator is wise, so it is not permissible for Him to create these things, because foolishness is impossible for Him. There is no doubt that they are originated, so they must have an originator. Thus we know that they have a foolish originator, and that is Ahriman. Likewise, the originator of evil is evil, and the Creator, exalted and high, is transcendent of this attribute. So it indicates that the existence of evil was by the creation of another, not by His creation.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage presents the doubt (shubah) of the Magians (Zoroastrians) regarding the duality of the Creator. They argue that since there are harmful, ugly, and disgusting things in the world, a wise Creator would not create such things because foolishness is impossible for Him. Therefore, these things must have a different originator who is foolish, and that is Ahriman. They further argue that the originator of evil must be evil, and since God is transcendent of evil, evil must be created by another being distinct from God.

Key Terms

إثنينية
أهر من
خالق
محدث
سفه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because evil exists, there must be an evil creator distinct from the good God.
Correction: The argument assumes evil is absolute and cannot be part of divine wisdom, which is not necessarily true. Evil may be relative or permitted for a greater good.

Checkpoint
What is the basis of the Magian doubt about the unity of the Creator?
A) The existence of evil and harmful things in the world
B) The existence of multiple gods
C) The lack of divine mercy
D) The impossibility of creation ex nihilo

Key Takeaway
The Magian argument for duality hinges on the claim that evil cannot originate from a wise creator, thus requiring a separate foolish creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face harm or ugliness in your own life, do you ever, even for a moment, question whether God truly is wise? What would it take for you to accuse God of foolishness?
?
The Magians concluded that evil must come from a separate creator. In your heart, have you ever subtly divided God's sovereignty, attributing good to Him but blaming evil on something else—like fate, people, or the devil? How does this lesson expose that tendency in you?
?
If you truly believed that everything in your life—including the painful, disgusting, and harmful—comes from the One Wise Creator, how would your response to suffering change starting today?

Refuting Magian Claims on Evil and Ahriman's Origin
Imam al-Nasafi dismantles the Magian narrative of evil's origin through a series of logical dilemmas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical inconsistencies in the Magian (Zoroastrian) account of evil and the origin of Ahriman, as exposed by Imam al-Nasafi's dialectical refutation.

Core Idea
Every explanation of the origin of evil leads to a contradiction if it compromises God's attributes.

This passage continues the refutation of the Magian dualist claim that evil originates from Ahriman while Yazdān is purely good. Imam al-Nasafi presses the Magians on their own premises, showing that their concept of the ancient light (Yazdān) is riddled with imperfections, and then examines every possible account of the thought that produced Ahriman, each leading to an absurdity. This lesson will walk through the dialectical moves.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the dialectical style: the author poses questions and follows each answer to a contradiction.
2
Identify the initial charge
The author first notes that Magians attribute ignorance, doubt, and weakness to Yazdān. If such imperfections are allowed, why not evil?
This sets the stage: the Magian concept of Yazdān is already compromised.
3
Follow the trilemma on the thought producing Ahriman
The author examines three possibilities for the thought that led to Ahriman: by Yazdān's choice, by forced action, or by itself. Each is shown to be problematic.
Track how each possibility undermines the Magian position.
4
Examine the final questions on knowledge and power
Even if the thought occurred by itself, the author asks whether Yazdān knew about it and could prevent it, leading to further contradictions.
These questions highlight the incoherence of the dualist framework.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how the refutation works by accepting Magian premises and showing they lead to absurd conclusions.
This method is a classic kalam technique: reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلنا : لهم لما جاز الجهل على النور القديم عندكم وجاز عليه الشك والهم والحاجة إلى طلب الولد، وجاز عليه العجز عن قهر عدوه حتى صالحه وهادئه جاز عليه الشر، وأي شر فوق هذه الشرور. ثم يقال لهم: تلك الشكة والفكرة التي حدث منها أهر من حدثت باختياره أم لا باختياره؟ فإن حدثت منه باختياره فمن أصل الشر، فإذا جاز منه إيجاد الشرور باختياره فلماذا لا يجوز إيجاد ما هو دونه من الشرور ؟ وإن حدثت لا باختياره (قيل: حدثت) بفعله الاضطراري أم بنفسها لا بفعل أحد ؟ فإن حدثت بفعله الاضطراري فهو إذا مضطر عاجز، إذ المضطر من يوجد غيره فيه فعلا، وكل من هو عاجز ومحل لمقدور غيره فهو محدث، فالقول إذا بقدم يزدان محال. وإن حدثت الفكرة بنفسها لا بفعل النور باختياره أو اضطراره فهو محال لما مر من استحالة حدوث حادث لا بإحداث أحد، ولو جاز ذا لجاز حدوث جميع العالم بنفسه، وبطلت الدلالة على الصانع، ثم لو وجدت الفكرة أو الشكة بنفسها هل كان القديم عالما بحدوثها أم لا؟ فإن قالوا : لا ، فقد جهلوه، والجهل لا يليق بالصانع القديم، وإن قالوا نعم قيل لهم هل كان قادرا على منعها عن الحدوث؟ فإن قالوا : لا ، فقد عجزوه وهو أيضا
We say: To them, since ignorance is permitted for the ancient light according to you, and doubt, worry, and need to seek offspring are permitted for it, and inability to overcome his enemy until he made peace and reconciled with him, then evil is permitted for him. And what evil is greater than these evils? Then it is said to them: That doubt and thought from which Ahriman originated - did it occur by his choice or not by his choice? If it occurred from him by his choice, then he is the origin of evil. So if the creation of evils by his choice is permitted for him, why is it not permitted for him to create what is lesser than these evils? And if it occurred not by his choice - it is said: did it occur by his forced action or by itself without the action of anyone? If it occurred by his forced action, then he is compelled and incapable, because the compelled is one in whom the action of another occurs, and everyone who is incapable and a locus for the power of another is originated. So the statement of the eternity of Yazdān is impossible. And if the thought occurred by itself without the action of the light by his choice or compulsion, then that is impossible due to what has passed of the impossibility of an originated event occurring without an originator. And if this were permitted, then the occurrence of the entire world by itself would be permitted, and the proof for the Maker would be invalidated. Then, if the thought or the doubt occurred by itself, was the ancient knowing of its occurrence or not? If they say: No, then they have made Him ignorant, and ignorance is not befitting for the ancient Maker. And if they say: Yes, it is said to them: Was He able to prevent it from occurring? If they say: No, then they have made Him incapable, and He is also...
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage continues the refutation by engaging the Magians on their own terms. The author points out that according to the Magians, their ancient light (Yazdān) is subject to ignorance, doubt, worry, and even weakness in needing offspring and making peace with his enemy. Therefore, if such imperfections are allowed for him, there is no reason why he cannot be the source of evil. The author then poses a series of pointed questions about the origin of the thought that produced Ahriman. If it occurred by Yazdān's choice, then he is the origin of evil. If not by his choice, then either it occurred by forced action (making him limited and thus not eternal) or by itself (which violates the principle that every event needs an originator). Finally, the author examines whether the ancient was aware of the thought and could prevent it, leading to dilemmas regarding knowledge and power. This dialectical method aims to force the Magians into contradictions.

Key Terms
نور قديم
يزدان
أهر من
شكة
فكرة
اضطرار
اختيار
عجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Magian view that Yazdān is purely good but impotent against Ahriman is consistent.
Correction: The refutation shows that any account of evil's origin either makes Yazdān the source of evil, contingent, or violates causality.

Checkpoint
What does the author argue about the thought that led to Ahriman's origin?
A) It must have occurred by Yazdān's choice
B) It must have occurred by forced action
C) It must have occurred by itself
D) Each possibility leads to a contradiction with the Magians' own claims

Key Takeaway
The Magian account of evil leads to logical contradictions that undermine their own claims about Yazdān.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Magians tried to protect their god from evil by claiming evil came from a separate being. But that led to admitting ignorance and weakness in their god. Where in your own heart have you tried to 'protect' Allah from the reality of evil, only to end up diminishing His sovereignty? Will you repent and affirm that He alone is the Creator of all, good and evil?
?
If a single doubt about Allah's perfection can lead to a cascade of contradictions, what does that say about the thoughts you entertain about Allah's justice and power in times of trial? Are you willing to silence every whisper that questions His perfect attributes?
?
The Magians’ system collapsed because they could not explain the origin of evil without violating causality. How often do you, in your daily struggles, try to explain evil in a way that subtly excuses you from trusting in Allah’s perfect decree? Will you commit today to submit to His decree even when you do not understand it?

The Dualist Claim and Their Three Sects
Nasafi introduces the dualist claim and enumerates their three sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the origin of the dualist doctrine, their belief in two eternal principles (light and darkness), and the three dualist sects mentioned by Imam Nasafi.

Core Idea
Dualism posits two eternal sources of good and evil, but splits into three distinct sects.

Imam Nasafi begins his refutation of dualism by tracing its origins to earlier heresies. The dualists, influenced by Materialists and Magians, claimed that the world arises from the mixture of two eternal principles: light and darkness. They attributed all good to light and all evil to darkness. Nasafi then identifies the three main dualist sects, setting the stage for their refutation.

Guided Path
1
Trace the origin of dualism
Read the first part of the passage to see how Nasafi explains that dualists borrowed ideas from the Materialists (al-Dahriyya) and the Magians (al-Majus). Notice what each group contributed.
The dualists combined these influences into their own system.
2
Identify the two eternal principles
The passage states that dualists affirmed two eternal principles: light and darkness. Understand how they describe their interaction and the resulting world.
All good is attributed to light, all evil to darkness.
3
List the three sects
Nasafi mentions three sects: the Manichaeans, the Daysanites, and the Marcionites. Commit these names to memory as they will be refuted individually later.
These are historical sects; focus on their classification here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣ - الكلام في إبطال قول الثنوية: ثم إن طائفة تلقنوا من الدهرية استحالة حدوث شيء لا من شيء ومن المجوس خروج إحداث الإفزاع والأهوال والآلام والأوجاع والشرور والأجسام الضارة والأجسام المستقذرة المستخبثة عن الحكمة فأثبتوا للعالم أصلين قديمين كانا لم يزل متباينين فامتزجا فحصل العالم من امتزاجهما وهما النور والظلمة أضافوا جميع ما في العالم من الخيرات والمسرات إلى النور وجميع ما فيه من الشرور والهموم والآلام والأحزان والإفزاع إلى الظلمة. وافترقت هذه الطائفة ثلاث فرق: أحدها: المانوية. والثانية: الديصانية والثالثة: المرقيونية.
3. Discourse on refuting the statement of the Dualists: Then a group learned from the Materialists (al-Dahriyya) the impossibility of something coming into existence from nothing, and from the Magians (al-Majus) the attribution of the production of terrifying things, horrors, pains, agonies, evils, harmful bodies, and disgusting, filthy bodies away from wisdom. So they affirmed for the world two eternal principles that have never ceased being distinct, then they mixed, and the world came into existence from their mixture, and they are light and darkness. They attributed all the good and pleasures in the world to light, and all the evils, griefs, pains, sorrows, and terrors in it to darkness. And this group split into three sects: one of them is the Manichaeans, the second is the Daysanites, and the third is the Marcionites.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage begins the refutation of dualism. Imam Nasafi first presents the origin of the dualist doctrine: they took the impossibility of something from nothing from the Materialists (al-Dahriyya) and the attribution of evil to a second principle from the Magians. They posited two eternal principles—light and darkness—that were distinct and then mixed, producing the world. All good comes from light, all evil from darkness. Then Nasafi enumerates the three sects of dualists: the Manichaeans (al-Manawiyya), the Daysanites (al-Dayṣāniyya), and the Marcionites (al-Marqiyūniyya). This classification sets up a detailed refutation of each.

Misconception: Some might think dualists are a single unified group.
Correction: Nasafi shows they are divided into three distinct sects: Manichaeans, Daysanites, and Marcionites.

Dualists claim two eternal principles (light and darkness) as sources of good and evil, and are divided into three sects: Manichaeans, Daysanites, and Marcionites.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The dualists thought that evil and suffering could not come from a wise God, so they invented a second source. When you face pain or injustice, does your heart ever whisper resentment against God, as if He were not in full control? Repent of that thought and affirm today that every hardship is from His wisdom and for your good.
?
The dualists borrowed ideas from Materialists and Magians rather than submitting to revelation. What ideas from the world around you — from friends, media, or your own assumptions — have you unconsciously mixed into your faith? Identify one and actively replace it with what Allah has taught you in this lesson.

The Manichaean Dualistic Cosmology
Nasafi details the Manichaean belief in two eternal principles, each with five elements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Manichaean doctrine of two eternal principles, light and darkness, and their five-fold structure.

Core Idea
Manichaeism teaches the world is built from two eternal, living principles: light and darkness.

The Manichaean sect, attributed to the prophet Mani, presents a radical dualism that challenged Islamic monotheism. In this passage, Imam Nasafi outlines their core belief: the universe is composed of two eternal principles, each with a five-part structure. Understanding this heresy is essential to grasping the arguments that will follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the full description of Manichaean dualism.
Notice the irregular derivation of the sect's name.
2
Identify the two principles
Note that light and darkness are described as living, hearing, seeing. What does this imply about their status?
Both are eternal and active.
3
Examine the five species
Each principle has five species: four bodies and one spirit. For light, the bodies are light, fire, wind, water; the spirit is the moving breeze.
4
Consider the theological challenge
Why does this dualism oppose the Islamic concept of Tawhid? Reflect on the implications of two eternal principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما المانوية فهم المنسوبون إلى ماني ويقال لهم: المنانية وهي نسبة على غير قياس كما يقال لأصحاب عاني من اليهود عنانية ومذهبه أن العالم متركب من أصلين قديمين: أحدهما النور والآخر الظلمة وهما جميعا حيان سميعان بصيران وكل واحد منهما خمسة أجناس أربعة من ذلك أبدان وواحد: فأما روح أبدان النور فهي النور والنار والريح والماء وروحه النسيم المتحرك في الأبدان
As for the Manichaeans, they are those attributed to Mani, and they are called al-Manāniyya, a non-standard attribution, just as the followers of ʿĀnī from the Jews are called ʿAnāniyya. His doctrine is that the world is composed of two eternal principles: one is light and the other is darkness, and both are living, hearing, seeing. Each of them has five species, four of them are bodies and one: as for the soul of the bodies of light, it is light, fire, wind, and water, and its spirit is the breeze moving in the bodies.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage explains the doctrine of the Manichaean sect. They are followers of Mani, and their name is an irregular derivation. Their belief is that the world is constituted from two eternal principles: light and darkness. Both principles are living, hearing, and seeing. Each principle consists of five species (or elements): four are bodies and one is the soul/spirit. For light, its bodies are light, fire, wind, and water, and its spirit is the moving breeze within these bodies. This description sets up the dualistic cosmology that Nasafi will refute.

Key Terms
ماني
المانوية
المنانية
النور
الظلمة
أصلين
خمسة أجناس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Manichaeans believe in two equal gods with identical attributes.
Correction: The passage states both principles are living, hearing, seeing, and eternal, but it does not state they are equal in power or goodness. The refutation will highlight the logical problems of dualism.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many species does each principle have in Manichaean doctrine?
A) Four
B) Five
C) Six
D) Three

Key Takeaway
Manichaeism posits two eternal, living principles—light and darkness—each comprising five elements, directly contradicting Islamic monotheism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever subconsciously treat evil as an independent force beyond Allah's control, rather than recognizing that everything happens by His will? How can you train your heart to see Allah's absolute sovereignty over both good and evil?
?
The Manichaeans believed light and darkness are 'living, hearing, seeing'—attributes that belong only to Allah. Is there anything in your life that you treat as if it has the power to hear you or see you besides Allah? What concrete step can you take today to redirect that reverence solely to Him?
?
The passage says darkness is eternal. In your own spiritual journey, have you given any 'darkness'—a habit, a thought, a relationship—a kind of eternal foothold in your life, as if it will never change? What is one thing you can do this week to affirm that only Allah is eternal and that darkness can be removed by His light?

The Dualist Claim and the Three Sects
Describes dualist claim and three sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dualist claim that the world originates from two eternal principles, light and darkness, and identify the three dualist sects: Manichaeans, Daysanites, and Marcionites.

Core Idea
Dualists reduce the world's complexity to a battle between light and darkness.

This passage begins by establishing the foundational belief of dualist sects: that the world arises from two eternal, distinct origins—light and darkness. All good and pleasure are from light; all evil and suffering from darkness. This worldview splits into three main sects, which the author names before delving into the Manichaean system.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once for overall meaning, then read the translation. Notice the structure: first the general claim, then the enumeration of sects.
Pay attention to the attribution of good and evil.
2
Identify the dualist claim
Find the two eternal principles and what is attributed to each. The text states that all good and pleasures go to light, all evils and sorrows to darkness.
3
List the three sects
The passage explicitly lists three sects: Manichaeans, Daysanites, and Marcionites. Note their names in Arabic.
These are the main groups within dualism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الضارة والأجسام المستقذرة المستخبثة عن الحكمة، فأثبتوا للعالم أصلين قديمين كانا لم يزل ،متباينين فامتزجا فحصل العالم من امتزاجهما، وهما النور والظلمة. أضافوا جميع ما في العالم من الخيرات والمسرات إلى النور، وجميع ما فيه من الشرور والهموم والآلام والأحزان والإفزاع إلى الظلمة. [فرق الثنوية] وافترقت هذه الطائفة ثلاث فرق: أحدها: المانوية. والثانية : الديصانية والثالثة : المرقيونية. [مذهب ماني] فأما المانوية فهم المنسوبون إلى ماني ويقال لهم: المنانية وهي نسبة على غير قياس، كما يقال لأصحاب عاني من اليهود عنانية، ومذهبه أن العالم متركب من أصلين قديمين: أحدهما النور والآخر الظلمة، وهما جميعا حيان سميعان بصیران وكل واحد منهما خمسة أجناس أربعة من ذلك أبدان وواحد : فأما روح أبدان النور فهي النور والنار والريح والماء وروحه النسيم المتحرك في الأبدان الأربعة. وأبدان الظلمة الحريق والظلمة والسموم والضباب وروحه الدخان. وامتزجت أبدان هذا بأبدان ذاك وكذا روحهما فحصل العالم من الامتزاج، واختلفت هؤلاء في علة الامتزاج، فزعم بعضهم أن سبب الامتزاج كان من الظلمة. وزعم سبب الامتزاج كان من النور، فامتزج بعض أجزائه ببعض أجزائها فحدث من الامتزاج العالم ، وبقي فوق العالم النور الخالص، فهو أبدا يسعى في تخليص ما احتبس من أجزائه في الظلمة فيستخلص شيئا فشيئا إلى أن لا يبقى منها في وثائق الظلمة شيء، فيعود الأمر على ما كان قبل الامتزاج فتتمتع به أجزاء النور المستخلصة باتصالها بعالم النور، وتنال ما فيه من اللذات والمسرات فيستمتع بذلك ويستريح عما كان ينال من الآلام والشرور في وثائق الظلمة، وتتأذى أجزاء الظلمة التي كانت مختلطة بالنور وهذا هو تفسير البعث والنشور وصورة الثواب والعقاب عندهم ولهم في بدء الخلق وماهية السماوات والأرضين والجبال والبحار هذيانات كثيرة لا معنى لإطالة الكتاب بذكرها أوردها أرباب المقالات في كتبهم.
The harmful and loathsome bodies [that are] deemed disgusting by wisdom, so they posited for the world two eternal origins that had never ceased, mutually distinct, then they intermixed and the world resulted from their intermixture, and they are light and darkness. They attributed all the good things and pleasures in the world to light, and all the evils, sorrows, pains, griefs, and terrors in it to darkness. [Sects of the Dualists] And this group split into three sects: one of them: the Manichaeans; the second: the Daysanites; and the third: the Marcionites. [Doctrine of Mani] As for the Manichaeans, they are those attributed to Mani, and they are called al-Mananiyya, a derivation irregularly, just as the followers of Ani among the Jews are called Ananiyya. His doctrine is that the world is composed of two eternal origins: one of them light and the other darkness, and both are living, hearing, seeing. Each of them has five genera: four of those are bodies and one is a spirit. As for the bodies of light, they are light, fire, wind, and water; and its spirit is the moving breeze in the four bodies. And the bodies of darkness are the burning, darkness, poison, and mist; and its spirit is smoke. And the bodies of this mixed with the bodies of that, and likewise their spirits, so the world resulted from the mixture. And they differed regarding the cause of the mixture; some claimed that the cause of the mixture was from darkness. And some claimed that the cause of the mixture was from light, so some of its parts mixed with some of its parts, and from the mixture the world occurred. And above the world remained pure light; it is ever striving to extract what of its parts is trapped in darkness, extracting little by little until none of them remains in the bonds of darkness, so the matter returns to what it was before the mixture, and the extracted parts of light enjoy through their connection to the world of light, and attain the pleasures and delights therein, enjoying that and resting from what they used to suffer of pains and evils in the bonds of darkness. And the parts of darkness that were mixed with light are harmed. This is their interpretation of resurrection and rising, and the form of reward and punishment according to them. And they have many delirious statements about the beginning of creation and the essence of the heavens, earths, mountains, and seas, the mention of which would be pointless to prolong the book; the authors of sectarian books have recorded them.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage describes the dualist sects and focuses on Manichaean cosmology. It begins by stating that the dualists (ثنوية) posited two eternal, distinct origins for the world: light (النور) and darkness (الظلمة), attributing all good to light and all evil to darkness. It then notes that this group split into three sects: Manichaeans (المانوية), Daysanites (الديصانية), and Marcionites (المرقيونية). The author then delves into the Manichaean doctrine, attributed to Mani. According to Mani, the world is composed of two eternal origins, both living, hearing, and seeing. Each origin has five genera (خمسة أجناس): four bodies (أبدان) and one spirit (روح). For light, the bodies are light, fire, wind, and water; its spirit is the moving breeze (النسيم المتحرك). For darkness, the bodies are burning (الحريق), darkness, poison (السموم), and mist (الضباب); its spirit is smoke (الدخان). The mixture of these bodies and spirits produced the world. The Manichaeans disagreed on the cause of this mixture: some said it originated from darkness, others from light. After mixture, pure light remained above the world and continuously works to extract its trapped parts from darkness until all are freed, restoring the original state. The extracted light parts then enjoy connection with the world of light, while the darkness parts suffer. This is their interpretation of resurrection, reward, and punishment. The author concludes that the Manichaeans had many absurd stories about creation, which he omits.

ثنوية
أصلان قديمان
نور
ظلمة
مانوية
ديصانية
مرقيونية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many dualist sects are mentioned in the passage?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Dualist sects share the belief that the world results from the mixture of two eternal principles, light and darkness, with all good from light and all evil from darkness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience pain or evil in your life, do you ever feel as though there is a separate force opposing God, subtly doubting that Allah alone is in control of all that happens? How can you train your heart to see even hardship as coming from His hand?
?
The dualists attributed all evil to darkness, removing responsibility from themselves. In what areas of your life have you blamed external sources for your struggles rather than examining your own heart and turning to Allah?
?
If someone told you that the world is a result of two equal powers, what would you say to them right now, based on this lesson? Would you be able to defend tawhid clearly, or do you feel a need to strengthen your understanding of Allah's sole sovereignty?

Manichaean Cosmology: Five Genera, Mixture, and Eschatology
Details Manichaean cosmology: five genera, mixture, and eschatology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Manichaean view of the world as a mixture of light and darkness, each with five genera, and their explanation of the ultimate separation and resurrection.

Core Idea
The world is a prison of light particles trapped in darkness, and salvation is their gradual extraction.

After naming the three dualist sects, the author details the Manichaean system. Mani taught that each eternal principle consists of four bodies and one spirit. Their mixture produced the world, and the ongoing process of extracting light from darkness defines their understanding of resurrection, reward, and punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the Manichaean passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the translation. Notice the detailed enumeration of genera and the narrative of mixture and extraction.
Focus on the five genera for each principle.
2
Identify the five genera
For light: bodies are light, fire, wind, water; spirit is moving breeze. For darkness: bodies are burning, darkness, poison, mist; spirit is smoke. List them.
3
Understand the cause of mixture
The passage mentions two views on what caused the mixture: some say darkness initiated it, others say light. Note this disagreement.
4
Trace the process of extraction and eschatology
Pure light gradually extracts trapped light parts from darkness. When all are freed, the original state is restored. This is their interpretation of resurrection and reward/punishment.
This is the core of Manichaean soteriology.

?

Daysanite Dualism: One Genus Each
Compares Daysanite and Manichaean dualism on unity of genera.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Daysanite doctrine of two eternal origins and how it differs from Manichaeism regarding the unity of genera.

Core Idea
Daysanites simplify dualism: light is one genus, darkness one genus.

The Daysanites are another dualist sect that, like the Manichaeans, posit two eternal origins: light and darkness. However, they differ in a crucial way: they see each origin as a single, unified genus. This lesson unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the similarity first, then the exception marker 'إلا أنهم يقولون'.
The passage compares Daysanites and Manichaeans side by side.
2
Identify the shared belief
Both sects agree on two eternal origins (light and darkness) and that good comes from light, evil from darkness.
This is the foundation of dualism.
3
Spot the difference
The Daysanites say light is wholly one genus and darkness is one genus. The Manichaeans, as earlier, divide each into five genera.
This is the key differentiator.
4
Apply the contrast
Reflect on why unity vs. multiplicity of genera matters for theological consistency.
Simpler dualism vs. complex dualism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفرقة الثانية الديصانية منهم وقولهم مثل قول المانوية في أصلين قديمين للعالم وهما النور والظلمة، فالخيرات كلها من النور، والشرور والآفات من الظلمة. [الفرق بين الديصانية والمانوية] إلا أنهم يقولون النور كله جنس واحد وكذلك الظلمة، والمانوية يجعلون كل
And the second sect, the Daysanites from among them, and their statement is like the statement of the Manichaeans concerning two eternal origins for the world, namely light and darkness; so all good things are from light, and all evils and afflictions are from darkness. [The difference between the Daysanites and the Manichaeans] Except that they say that light is entirely one genus, and likewise darkness, while the Manichaeans make each...
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents the Daysanite (الديصانية) sect as the second group of dualists. The author states that their doctrine resembles that of the Manichaeans regarding there being two eternal origins for the world: light and darkness; all good originates from light, all evil and afflictions from darkness. However, the key difference (الفرق بين الديصانية والمانوية) is that the Daysanites consider light to be one single genus (جنس واحد) and similarly darkness one genus, whereas the Manichaeans, as previously described, divide each of light and darkness into five genera (four bodies and one spirit). The text ends mid-sentence, but the contrast is clear: the Daysanites hold a simpler dualism compared to the complex fivefold structure of the Manichaeans.

Key Terms

مانوية
نور
ظلمة
جنس واحد
خيرات
شرور
آفات
أصلان قديمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Daysanites and Manichaeans are identical in all respects.
Correction: They differ on the unity of the genera: Daysanites say each origin is one genus; Manichaeans divide each into five.

Checkpoint
What is the main difference between the Daysanites and the Manichaeans according to this passage?
A) Daysanites believe in three eternal origins, while Manichaeans believe in two.
B) Daysanites say light and darkness are each one genus, while Manichaeans divide each into five genera.
C) Daysanites attribute all evil to light, while Manichaeans attribute it to darkness.
D) Daysanites believe the world was created ex nihilo, while Manichaeans believe in mixture.

Key Takeaway
Daysanites and Manichaeans share a dualistic framework, but differ on whether each principle is a single genus or subdivided.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you ever subconsciously think that good comes only from one source (e.g., your own efforts) and evil from another (e.g., others or circumstances)? How does this dualistic mindset undermine your reliance on Allah as the sole Creator and Controller of all things? This week, when you face a setback, consciously say 'This is from Allah' and seek His wisdom rather than blaming an external source.
?
The Daysanites believed light is one undivided good and darkness is one undivided evil. How might a similarly simplistic view of people—labeling them as entirely 'good' or entirely 'bad'—prevent you from seeing the complexity of human nature and from showing mercy as Allah commands? Challenge yourself to find something good in someone you have written off.
?
If you had to explain to a friend why dividing light and darkness into multiple genera (as Manichaeans do) still leads to a flawed belief in two gods, what would you say? How does your own heart sometimes 'divide' causes and effects between Allah and secondary agents, thereby diminishing your tawheed? Make a firm intention to attribute every outcome—good or difficult—directly to Allah.

Manichaean Cosmology and Eschatology
Describes Manichaean cosmology: bodies of darkness, mixing, and eschatology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Manichaean doctrine of two eternal principles (light and darkness), their mixing that produced the world, and their eschatological process of liberating light particles from darkness.

Core Idea
In Manichaeism, the world is a mixture of light and darkness, and salvation is the gradual liberation of light.

Imam al-Nasafi presents the Manichaean cosmology as part of his refutation of dualist sects. This passage outlines their view of primordial mixing, the ongoing process of liberation, and their reinterpretation of resurrection and reward. Understanding this prepares you to appreciate the Islamic critique of such dualistic systems.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how the Manichaeans describe the bodies of darkness and the mixing process.
Pay attention to the dispute over the cause of mixing.
2
Identify key components
Break down the passage into parts: the list of darkness elements, the mixing, the dispute over cause, the liberation process, and the eschatology.
This will help you see the structure of their belief.
3
Compare with Islamic monotheism
Reflect on how this dualistic view differs from Islamic tawhid, especially regarding creation, good and evil, and the afterlife.
This is the broader theological context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأربعة. وأبدان الظلمة الحريق والظلمة والسموم والضباب وروحه الدخان. وامتزجت أبدان هذا بأبدان ذاك وكذا روحهما فحصل العالم من الامتزاج، واختلفت هؤلاء في علة الامتزاج، فزعم بعضهم أن سبب الامتزاج كان من الظلمة. وزعم سبب الامتزاج كان من النور، فامتزج بعض أجزائه ببعض أجزائها أن فحدث من الامتزاج العالم، وبقي فوق العالم النور الخالص، فهو أبدا يسعى في تخليص ما احتبس من أجزائه في الظلمة فيستخلص شيئا فشيئا إلى أن لا يبقى منها في وثائق الظلمة شيء، فيعود الأمر على ما كان قبل الامتزاج فتتمتع به أجزاء النور المستخلصة باتصالها بعالم النور، وتنال ما فيه من اللذات والمسرات فيستمتع بذلك ويستريح عما كان ينال من الآلام والشرور في وثائق الظلمة، وتتأذى أجزاء الظلمة التي كانت مختلطة بالنور وهذا هو تفسير البعث والنشور وصورة الثواب والعقاب عندهم ولهم في بدء الخلق وماهية السماوات والأرضين والجبال والبحار هذيانات كثيرة لا معنى لإطالة الكتاب بذكرها أوردها أرباب المقالات في كتبهم.
The four. And the bodies of darkness: fire, darkness, poison, fog, and its spirit is smoke. And the bodies of this mixed with the bodies of that, and likewise their spirits, so the world came about from the mixing. And these differed concerning the cause of the mixing. Some of them claimed that the cause of the mixing was from darkness. And some claimed the cause of the mixing was from light. So some of its parts mixed with some of its parts, and thus the world came into existence from the mixing. And above the world remained pure light. It continuously strives to liberate what is imprisoned of its parts in darkness, extracting them little by little until nothing of them remains in the bonds of darkness. Then the matter returns to what it was before the mixing. So the liberated parts of light enjoy themselves by their connection to the world of light, attaining the pleasures and delights therein, and they rejoice and rest from the pains and evils they used to experience in the bonds of darkness. And the parts of darkness that were mixed with light suffer. And this is their interpretation of resurrection and dispersal, and the form of reward and punishment according to them. And they have many deliriums about the beginning of creation and the nature of the heavens, earths, mountains, and seas, the mention of which does not warrant prolonging the book; the authors of articles have mentioned them in their books.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents the Manichaean doctrine of two eternal principles, light and darkness, and their cosmogony. It begins by listing the four (or five) bodies of darkness: fire, darkness, poison, fog, and their spirit, smoke. It then explains that the bodies and spirits of light and darkness mixed, resulting in the world. The Manichaeans differed on the cause: some said darkness initiated the mixing, others said light. The process of liberation is described: pure light above the world continually extracts its imprisoned parts from the bonds of darkness until none remain. After liberation, light particles reunite with the world of light and enjoy eternal pleasures, while the darkness parts suffer. This is their interpretation of resurrection and reward/punishment. The author dismisses their other myths as deliriums not worth mentioning.

Misconception: Manichaeans are purely dualistic with no interaction between light and darkness.
Correction: The passage shows they believe light and darkness mix, producing the world, and salvation is the separation of the mixture.

C) The liberation of light particles from darkness and their reunion with the world of light.

Key Takeaway

?

?

What is one action you will take today to demonstrate that your salvation depends on your obedience to Allah, not a cosmic process?
?
Notice how the Manichaeans disagreed on whether the cause of mixing came from light or darkness—they were confused about the origin of evil. When you face evil in your own life, do you ever blame external forces (like shaytan or others) while neglecting your own responsibility? Where do you need to stop shifting blame and sincerely repent to Allah, taking accountability for your choices?

Daysanite and Manichaean Dualism Compared
Compares Daysanite and Manichaean dualist beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key differences between the Daysanite and Manichaean dualist systems regarding the nature of light and darkness and the cause of their mixing.

Core Idea
Two dualist sects, one key difference: choice vs. nature.

The Daysanites and Manichaeans both believed in two eternal principles (light and darkness), but they disagreed on fundamental details. This passage from Imam Nasafi clarifies their contrasting views on whether darkness is active or passive, and why the mixing occurred. Understanding these nuances is crucial for recognizing the diversity within dualist thought.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the common ground first: both sects affirm two eternal principles.
The passage starts with the shared belief before introducing differences.
2
Identify the first difference: number of genera
The Daysanites say light and darkness are each one genus; the Manichaeans divide each into five genera. This is a structural difference in their cosmologies.
3
Identify the second difference: nature of darkness
For Daysanites, light is living and acts by choice, darkness is dead and acts by nature. Manichaeans claim both are living and act by choice.
This difference affects how they explain evil and free will.
4
Understand the Daysanite cause of mixing
Daysanites say light was disturbed by darkness's roughness and tried to repel it, becoming entangled. As a result, light is compelled to do evil while trapped.
This explains why evil exists in the world.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider how each sect's view of darkness (passive vs. active) leads to different explanations for the origin of evil.
This connects to the broader theological problem of evil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفرقة الثانية الديصانية منهم وقولهم مثل قول المانوية في أصلين قديمين للعالم وهما النور والظلمة، فالخيرات كلها من النور، والشرور والآفات من الظلمة. [الفرق بين الديصانية والمانوية] إلا أنهم يقولون النور كله جنس واحد وكذلك الظلمة، والمانوية يجعلون كل واحد منهما خمسة أجناس على ما بينا وكذا عند الديصانية النور حي يفعل ما يفعل باختياره، والظلمة موات عاجزة تفعل ما تفعل من الشرور بطباعها، والمانوية يزعمون أن كل واحد منها حي مختار يفعل ما يفعل باختياره، وزعم هؤلاء أن سبب الامتزاج كان من النور فإنه كان يتأذى بمجاورة الظلمة ومماستها وخشونتها فأراد دفعها فارتبك فيها، ويزعمون أن النور ما دام في وثائق الظلمة يفعل القبيح مضطرا، وبعد الخلاص لا يفعل ذلك.
And the second sect: the Daysanites. Their statement is like the statement of the Manichaeans concerning two eternal principles of the world, which are light and darkness. All good things are from light, and evils and afflictions are from darkness. [The difference between the Daysanites and the Manichaeans] But they say that light is entirely one genus, and likewise darkness. The Manichaeans make each one of them five genera, as we have explained. And likewise, according to the Daysanites, light is living, doing what it does by choice, and darkness is dead, incapable, doing what it does of evils by its nature. The Manichaeans claim that each of them is living, choosing, doing what it does by choice. And these (Daysanites) claimed that the cause of the mixing was from light, for it was harmed by the proximity, contact, and roughness of darkness, so it wanted to repel it and became entangled in it. And they claim that as long as light is in the bonds of darkness, it does evil under compulsion, and after liberation it does not do that.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage outlines the beliefs of the Daysanite sect and contrasts them with Manichaeans. Both believe in two eternal principles: light (source of good) and darkness (source of evil). The key difference is: Daysanites consider each principle as a single genus, whereas Manichaeans divide each into five genera. Furthermore, Daysanites assert that light is living and acts by will, while darkness is inert and acts by nature (by instinct). Manichaeans, on the other hand, hold that both are living and act by choice. The passage also explains the Daysanite view on the cause of the mixing: light was disturbed by darkness's proximity and roughness and tried to repel it, resulting in entanglement. In this state, light is compelled to do evil, but after liberation it ceases.

Correction: This passage shows they differ on the number of genera, the nature of darkness (dead vs. living), and the cause of mixing.

B) Dead and acting by nature.

The Daysanites viewed darkness as inert and acting by nature, while Manichaeans saw both principles as living and choosing; they also differed on the cause of mixing.

?
The Manichaeans gave darkness its own will, equal to light. Is there any 'darkness' in your life—a habit, a desire, a person—that you have begun to treat as an independent force that you cannot overcome? The Marcionite Third Principle: Neither Good nor Evil
Explains the Marcionite addition of a third neutral principle between light and darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Marcionites modified dualism by positing a third neutral principle between light and darkness, and its role in their cosmology.

Core Idea
Marcionites added a neutral 'equalizer' between light and darkness, making their dualism unique.

The Marcionites agreed with other dualist sects on two eternal principles, light and darkness. However, they uniquely introduced a third principle that is neither good nor evil, serving as a spatial and ontological buffer between the two. This passage explains the nature of this third principle and how it led to the creation of the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the Marcionites are described as a third sect among dualists.
2
Identify the three principles
Find light, darkness, and the third intermediate principle. Note how each is characterized: light as good, darkness as evil, and the third as neither.
The third is called 'al-mu`addil' (the equalizer).
3
Understand the spatial arrangement
Light is above, darkness below, and the third is between them. Each is finite in the direction they meet and infinite in the other five directions.
Marcionites differ from Manichaeans and Daysanites in positing a barrier.
4
Follow the cosmological narrative
Darkness attacks the third principle, mixes with it, and from this mixture the world is built. Light then sends a spirit (spirit of God) into the world.
This explains the origin of the world in Marcionite thought.
5
Compare with other dualist views
Notice how Marcionites differ from Manichaeans and Daysanites: those two had no barrier between light and darkness in eternity, whereas Marcionites have a third intermediate.
This distinction is key to understanding Marcionite uniqueness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفرقة الثالثة المرقيونية وهم يقولون بأصلين قديمين أحدهما النور والآخر الظلمة، وتفردوا بإثبات ثالث سليم ليس بخير كالنور ولا شرير كالظلمة، وهو متوسط بين النور والظلمة أسفل من النور وأعلى من الظلمة إذ من مذهبهم جميعا أن النور كان جهة العلو والظلمة كانت في جهة السفل، وكل واحد منها غير متناهي من خمس جهات متناهي من الجهة التي تلاقي بها صاحبه فالنور متناهي من جهة السفل والظلمة متناهية من جهة العلو، إلا أن عند المانوية والديصانية لم يكن بينها حائل في الأزل، وكان كل واحد منهما يلاقي صاحبه بجهة. وقالت المرقيونية : بل كان بينهما ثالث متوسط، لم يكن خيرا ولا شريرا ويسمونه المعدل، وقالوا : فتعدت الظلمة على هذا المتوسط فمازجته ثم بني العالم من ذلك المزاج لتطيب بذلك وتتلذ به فلما رأى النور ذلك بعث روحا إلى هذا العالم، وهو روح الله.
And the third sect: the Marcionites. They affirm two eternal principles, one of which is light and the other darkness. And they were unique in affirming a third (principle) that is sound, neither good like light nor evil like darkness, and it is intermediate between light and darkness, lower than light and higher than darkness. For according to all of them, light was in the direction of above and darkness was in the direction of below. Each one of them is infinite from five directions, finite from the direction in which it meets its companion. So light is finite from the direction of below, and darkness is finite from the direction of above. But according to the Manichaeans and Daysanites, there was no barrier between them in eternity, and each one met its companion in a direction. The Marcionites said: rather, there was between them a third intermediate, which was neither good nor evil, and they call it the equalizer (al-mu`addil). And they said: darkness transgressed against this intermediate, mixed with it, then the world was built from that mixture so that it (darkness) might be pleased and delighted thereby. When light saw that, it sent a spirit to this world, and it is the spirit of God.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents the Marcionite version of dualism. They agree with the other sects on two eternal principles (light and darkness) but uniquely posit a third neutral entity that is neither good nor evil, called 'al-mu`addil' (the equalizer). It is located spatially between light (above) and darkness (below). The passage explains the spatial extent: both light and darkness are infinite in five directions but finite where they face each other. Unlike Manichaeans and Daysanites who held direct contact from eternity, Marcionites assert a barrier third principle. Darkness attacked this third, mixed with it, and from that mixture the world was built for darkness's enjoyment. Upon witnessing this, light sent a spirit (identified as the spirit of God) into the world.

Key Terms
المرقيونية
الثالث المتوسط
المعدل

الظلمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Marcionites are simply dualists like Manichaeans.
Correction: Marcionites uniquely add a third neutral principle between light and darkness, distinguishing their cosmology.

Checkpoint
What is the role of the third principle (al-mu`addil) in Marcionite cosmology?
A) It is the source of evil.
B) It mediates between light and darkness and was attacked by darkness.
C) It is identical to light.
D) It creates the world intentionally.

Key Takeaway
The Marcionites introduced a neutral third principle that was attacked by darkness, leading to the mixture from which the world was formed, and light responded by sending a spirit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you ever try to maintain a 'neutral' position between right and wrong, hoping to avoid the consequences of either? What does the Marcionite error—inventing a third principle to separate light from darkness—teach you about the danger of creating such a middle ground in your own soul?
?
The Marcionites believed that darkness attacked the neutral principle, causing the world's mixture of good and evil. Have you ever attributed your own spiritual struggles to 'neutral' circumstances or people, rather than examining your own heart's response to God's truth? What would it look like to accept full responsibility before Him?
?
Light sent a spirit into the world after seeing darkness's aggression. How does this story challenge you to consider whether you are responding to evil with passive neutrality or with active, costly engagement—as light did?

Views of the Manichaeans and Daysaniyya on Light and Darkness
Describes dualist beliefs about light and darkness and the cause of mixing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key differences between the Daysaniyya and Manichaean dualist beliefs regarding light and darkness, and the Manichaean explanation for their mixing.

Core Idea
Dualist sects differ on whether darkness acts by nature or by choice, and why light became entangled in darkness.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents the views of two dualist sects: the Daysaniyya and the Manichaeans. Both believe in two principles—light and darkness—but they differ on the nature of darkness and the cause of their mixing. Understanding these views helps us see the variety of dualist thought and the refutations that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once, then its translation. Notice how the author distinguishes between the two sects.
The text uses 'وكذا عند الديصانية' to introduce the first view.
2
Identify the three doctrinal points
For each sect, observe their view on (1) the nature of light (living or dead), (2) the nature of darkness (powerless or active), and (3) the cause of mixing.
3
Analyze the Manichaean cause of mixing
Focus on why light tried to repel darkness and what resulted. This is key to understanding their dualism.
The light's entrapment explains why evil exists in the world.
4
Compare the sects
Create a mental or written comparison of the Daysaniyya and Manichaeans on the points identified. Notice the difference in the active/passive nature of darkness.
This comparison is the backbone of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحد منهما خمسة أجناس على ما بينا وكذا عند الديصانية النور حي يفعل (ما يفعل) باختياره، والظلمة موات عاجزة تفعل ما تفعل من الشرور بطباعها، والمانوية يزعمون أن كل واحد منها حي مختار يفعل ما يفعل باختياره، وزعم هؤلاء أن سبب الامتزاج كان من النور فإنه كان يتأذى بمجاورة الظلمة ومماستها وخشونتها فأراد دفعها فارتبك فيها، ويزعمون أن النور ما دام في وثائق الظلمة يفعل القبيح مضطرا، وبعد الخلاص لا يفعل ذلك.
One of them (has) five kinds according to what we explained, and likewise according to the Daysaniyya: the light is a living being that does what it does by choice, and the darkness is dead and powerless, doing what it does of evils by its nature. The Manichaeans claim that each of them is a living being with choice, doing what it does by choice. These (Manichaeans) claimed that the cause of mixing was from the light, for it was harmed by the proximity, contact, and roughness of the darkness, so it wanted to repel it and became entangled in it. They claim that as long as the light is in the bonds of darkness, it does evil under compulsion, but after deliverance it does not do that.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage describes the beliefs of two dualist sects: the Daysaniyya and the Manichaeans. It begins by noting that one of the two principles (light or darkness) according to each sect has five kinds, referring to an earlier classification. The Daysaniyya believe light is alive and acts by choice, while darkness is dead and powerless, causing evil by its nature. The Manichaeans, in contrast, believe both light and darkness are living and choose their actions. They also explain the cause of mixing: the light, disturbed by the proximity and roughness of darkness, tried to repel it and became entangled. Consequently, while trapped in darkness, the light is compelled to do evil, but once freed, it no longer does so.

The Marquiyuniyya: A Third Principle Between Light and Darkness
Presents the Marquiyuniyya's distinctive belief in a third medium between light and darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Marquiyuniyya sect's distinctive belief in a third intermediate being between light and darkness and their mythological account of creation.

Core Idea
The Marquiyuniyya added a neutral third being between light and darkness.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi introduces us to the third dualist sect, the Marquiyuniyya. While they share the belief in two eternal principles of light and darkness, they diverge by positing a third intermediate being that is neither good nor evil. This passage explains their unique cosmology and how they account for the creation of the world through the mixing of darkness with this intermediate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage twice
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation for overall flow. Then read again, noting the distinct beliefs of the Marquiyuniyya.
Pay attention to the spatial descriptions of light and darkness.
2
Identify the three principles
Find the light, darkness, and the 'moderator' (al-mu'addil). Notice how the moderator is described as neither good nor evil and intermediate in position.
3
Compare with other dualists
The text contrasts the Marquiyuniyya with the Manichaeans and Daysaniyya. Note the difference: the latter believe no barrier existed between light and darkness, while the Marquiyuniyya affirm a third intermediate separating them.
4
Understand the myth of creation and salvation
The passage narrates how darkness attacked the intermediate, causing a mixture from which the world was formed, and how light sent a spirit (Jesus) to rescue followers.
The denial of separation and mixing as distinct realities at the end is a subtle metaphysical point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفرقة الثالثة المرقيونية وهم يقولون بأصلين قديمين أحدهما النور والآخر الظلمة، وتفردوا بإثبات ثالث سليم ليس بخير كالنور ولا شرير كالظلمة، وهو متوسط بين النور والظلمة أسفل من النور وأعلى من الظلمة إذ من مذهبهم جميعا أن النور كان جهة العلو والظلمة كانت في جهة السفل، وكل واحد منها غير متناهي من خمس جهات متناهي من الجهة التي تلاقي بها صاحبه فالنور متناهي من جهة السفل والظلمة متناهية من جهة العلو، إلا أن عند المانوية والديصانية لم يكن بينها حائل في الأزل، وكان كل واحد منهما يلاقي صاحبه بجهة. وقالت المرقيونية : بل كان بينهما ثالث متوسط، لم يكن خيرا ولا شريرا ويسمونه المعدل، وقالوا : فتعدت الظلمة على هذا المتوسط فمازجته ثم () بني العالم من ذلك المزاج لتطيب بذلك وتتلذ به فلما رأى النور ذلك بعث روحا إلى هذا العالم، وهو روح الله وابنه عيسى فمن تبعه ولم يقرب النساء ولا الزهويات، أفلت من حبائل الظلمة، وأكثرهم ينكرون أن يكون التباين معنى (وراء المتباين أو الامتزاج معنى وراء الممتزج) لم ينعدم عند الامتزاج معنى هو التباين ولا حدث معنى هو الامتزاج.
And the third sect is the Marquiyuniyya. They affirm two eternal principles: one is light and the other darkness. They uniquely affirm a third sound (principle) that is neither good like the light nor evil like the darkness, and it is intermediate between light and darkness, below the light and above the darkness, because according to all of them, the light was in the direction of above and the darkness was in the direction of below, and each of them is infinite from five directions and finite from the direction in which it meets its companion. So the light is finite from the direction of below, and the darkness is finite from the direction of above. However, according to the Manichaeans and the Daysaniyya, there was no barrier between them in pre-eternity, and each of them met its companion by a direction. The Marquiyuniyya said: Rather, there was between them a third intermediate, which was neither good nor evil, and they call it the 'moderator'. They said: The darkness transgressed against this intermediate and mixed with it, then () was built the world from that mixture so that it (the darkness) might become good and enjoy it. When the light saw that, it sent a spirit to this world, and it is the spirit of God and His son Jesus. Whoever follows him and does not approach women nor falsehood, escapes from the snares of darkness. Most of them deny that separation is a meaning beyond the separated or that mixing is a meaning beyond the mixed. (They claim that) when mixing occurs, the meaning of separation is not annihilated, nor does a meaning of mixing come into existence.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage presents the third dualist sect, the Marquiyuniyya, and their distinctive belief. They also affirm two eternal principles (light and darkness) but uniquely add a third intermediary being that is neither good nor evil. The passage describes the spatial arrangement: light is above, darkness below, each infinite in five directions but finite where they meet. Unlike the Manichaeans and Daysaniyya, the Marquiyuniyya maintain that in pre-eternity there was a barrier (the third intermediate) between them. This intermediate, called al-mu'addil (the moderator), was attacked by darkness, resulting in a mixture from which the world was formed. The light then sent a spirit (identified as the Spirit of God and Jesus Christ) to the world to rescue those who follow him by abstaining from women and falsehoods. The passage ends by noting that most Marquiyuniyya deny that separation and mixing are distinct realities beyond the objects themselves; they claim that mixing does not destroy the meaning of separation nor create a new meaning of mixing.

Key Terms
المرقيونية
النور
الظلمة
المعدل
التباين
الامتزاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Marquiyuniyya are identical to the Manichaeans in their dualism.
Correction: The Marquiyuniyya uniquely add a third intermediate principle between light and darkness, which neither Manichaeans nor Daysaniyya affirm.

Checkpoint
What unique belief distinguishes the Marquiyuniyya from other dualist sects?
A) They believe light is alive and darkness is dead.
B) They affirm a third intermediate being that is neither good nor evil.
C) They believe light and darkness are both eternal and self-sufficient.
D) They deny the existence of darkness.

Key Takeaway
The Marquiyuniyya deviated from standard dualism by introducing a neutral third mediating principle between light and darkness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This sect believed in a neutral, third being between good and evil. Have you ever found yourself acting as a 'moderator' between truth and falsehood, trying to stay neutral when Allah commands clarity? Where in your life are you refusing to take a stand for tawhid because it feels safer to be neither 'good' nor 'evil'?
?
The Marquiyuniyya taught that salvation came through following Jesus and avoiding women and falsehood. Are there any teachings or practices you hold that are not from the Quran and Sunnah, but that you rely on for spiritual safety? What would it cost you to abandon them and rely solely on Allah's guidance?
?
They claimed that the world was built from a mixture of darkness and the moderator, and that light responded by sending a spirit. When you examine your own life, do you sometimes attribute events to a mixture of good and evil sources, forgetting that Allah alone is the Creator and that nothing happens outside His will? In what specific situation yesterday did you fail to see Allah's sole control?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
6 min
Separation and Mixture as Proof of Origination
Author proves separation and mixture are accidents, refuting dualists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author proves that separation and mixture are originated accidents, thereby refuting the dualist claim that light and darkness are eternal.

Core Idea
Separation and mixture are observable accidents, proving light and darkness are not eternal.

This lesson examines a key argument against the dualist belief that light and darkness are eternal principles. The author shows that separation and mixture are accidents that occur in these two bodies, and since they are originated, the bodies themselves must be originated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation once to get the overall argument without analyzing deeply.
Notice how the author builds on previously established proofs.
2
Identify the two key claims
Identify the two main claims: (1) separation and mixture are meanings beyond the substances, and (2) mixture is perceived in sensation, separation by its susceptibility to non-existence, so both are originated.
3
Understand the logical principle
The author applies the principle: 'whatever does not precede the originated is itself originated.' Since light and darkness are never free from separation and mixture, they cannot precede them, so they are also originated.
This principle is central to the proof.
4
Connect to refutation of dualists
Reflect on how this argument undermines the dualist position by showing that light and darkness are not eternal but originated, thus rejecting dualism.
The author also references earlier discussions on creation from nothing and the problem of evil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[فساد كلام الثنوية] وما أقمنا من الدلالة على ثبوت الأعراض فهو الدليل على كون التباين والامتزاج معنيين وراء ذاتيهما، وقد حدث الامتزاج في الحس، وعرف حدوث التباين بقبول العدم، فكانا معنيين حادثين، والنور والظلمة لا يخلوان عنهما ولا يسبقانهما، وقد مر أن ما لا يسبق الحادث فهو حادث، وكل دلیل عرف به حدوث سائر الأجسام فذلك الدليل موجود في حق هذين الجسمين، وقد سبق في الكلام ما يدل على جواز وجود الشيء لا من شيء، وعلى جواز إيجاد القبيح وكونه حكمة عند تعلق العاقبة الحميدة به على ما مر في إبطال كلام المجوس.
[Refutation of the Dualists’ Discourse] And what we have established as proof for the subsistence of accidents is the evidence that separation and mixture are two meanings besides their substances. Mixture is perceived to occur in sensation, and separation is known to occur by its susceptibility to non-existence, so they are two originated meanings. Light and darkness are never free from them nor do they precede them. It has already passed that whatever does not precede the originated is itself originated. And every proof by which the origination of other bodies is known—that proof exists with respect to these two bodies. And there has already preceded in the discourse what indicates the permissibility of a thing coming to be from nothing, and the permissibility of creating evil and its being wisdom when a praiseworthy consequence is attached to it, as has passed in refuting the discourse of the Magians.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a proof that separation and mixture are accidents (meanings) that are originated, forming part of the refutation of dualists. The author first states that the argument used to establish the existence of accidents in general serves as evidence that separation and mixture are distinct meanings (i.e., accidents) beyond the substances in which they inhere. Then he notes that mixture is observed to occur in sensation, and separation is known to occur because it can cease to exist, so both are originated. Since light and darkness are never devoid of them and do not precede them, they are also originated. The author then invokes the general principle that whatever does not precede an originated thing is itself originated, and applies the same proofs used for other bodies to light and darkness. Finally, he references earlier discussions on the permissibility of creation from nothing and of evil accompanied by a good outcome, as used against the Magians, to reinforce the argument.

Key Terms
التباين
الامتزاج
الأعراض
الحادث
النور
الظلمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage is about the inherent nature of light and darkness as eternal.
Correction: The passage does not discuss the nature of light and darkness per se; it uses separation and mixture as accidents to prove that light and darkness are originated, thus refuting dualism.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how do we know that separation and mixture are originated meanings?
A) From textual revelation
B) Because mixture is perceived in sensation and separation is known by its susceptibility to non-existence
C) Because they are eternal in light and darkness
D) Because they are inseparable from bodies

Key Takeaway
Separation and mixture are observable, originated accidents; thus light and darkness, which never exist without them, must also be originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author proves that light and darkness are not eternal because they are never free from originated accidents. Consider something in your life that you assume is permanent or unchanging—a habit, a relationship, a fear. Is it truly free from change and contingency? How does realizing its originated nature change your attachment to it?
?
If even the principles of light and darkness—which many consider fundamental—are shown to be created and dependent, what does that mean for your own sense of self-sufficiency? Are you living as if you are self-originated, or do you acknowledge your contingency before the Creator?
?
The passage references the permissibility of evil with a praiseworthy consequence. Is there a trial in your life that you have resisted seeing as potentially bringing wisdom? Can you entrust its outcome to the All-Wise even when you cannot perceive the wisdom?
